<p>5. RestrictionsThe preliminary work has been published in IWFHR&#39;06 (The full text is available as draft version in local site or final versions in the publishing website ). Moreover, the expanded version is published as an original paper of IJDAR by Springer publisher. If you are using HIT-MW database in your paper, please refer to following references: </p>

<p>  </p>

<p>1. Tonghua Su, Tianwen Zhang, and Dejun Guan. &quot;Corpus-based HIT-MW database for offline recognition of general-purpose Chinese handwritten text&quot;. International Journal of Document Analysis and Recognition, 2007, 10(1): 27-38. </p>

<p>  </p>

<p>2. Tonghua Su, Tianwen Zhang, and Dejun Guan. &quot;HIT-MW Dataset for Offline Chinese Handwritten Text Recognition&quot;. Proceedings of the Tenth International Workshop on Frontiers in Handwriting Recognition, 2006. </p>

 title : The hitswdatabase Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>HIT-SW database is to facilitate the offline recognition of writer-dependent Chinese handwritten text. You can download it freely here. 1 OverviewA database of Chinese handwritten document is collected by our institute to evaluate the recognizer. It is written by a single writer, therefore we name it HIT-SW database (HIT is the abbr. of Harbin Institute of Technology, and SW means it is produced by a single writer) hence after. The homepage of HIT-SW database in English is http://hitswdb.googlepages.com/ and the Chinese version is put at http://hi.baidu.com/hitmw/ . </p>

<p>  </p>

<p>The underlying text of HIT-SW database is randomly sampled from China Daily corpus. We ask the writer to handcopy the text with no ruler as reference on A4 size papers. The final samples are digitalized with a resolution of 300 DPI, and then binarized using Otsu algorithm. Totally there are 83 handwritten documents capturing some important aspect of real handwriting, such as miswriting, erasure, character touching, document skewness et al. A counterpart database produced by multiple writers (HIT-MW database) had already released at http://hitmwdb.googlepages.com . </p>

<p>  </p>

<p>In our text line separation system, the global projection profile is executed to extract the straight border lines. However we find it unsatisfactory. Then we perform skew correction to improve the recall rate of text lines. After that, global projection profile is performed again. Using this technique, all of 798 text lines are succesfully extracted.  We randomly draw 200 of them as test set (4,926 characters), 500 as train set (12,670 characters), and the remainders as validation set (1,470 characters). The validation set here is used to tune the parameters which will be used to evaluate the recognizer&#39;s performance on test set.  </p>

<p>  </p>

<p>2 DownloadThe documents of HIT-SW Database can be downloaded freely below (with no commercial use):  </p>

<p>http://hitswdb.googlepages.com/HITSW.zip or http://hitswdatabase.googlecode.com/files/HITSW.zip (Size: 3.66 MB) </p>

<p>  </p>

<p>The filename of the extracted textline is based on the filename of the corresponding sample. These text lines can be downloaded below (no commercial use is certified yet): </p>

<p>http://hitswdb.googlepages.com/train.zip or http://hitswdatabase.googlecode.com/files/train.zip (Size: 2.32 MB) </p>

<p>http://hitswdb.googlepages.com/validation.zip or http://hitswdatabase.googlecode.com/files/validation.zip (Size: 468 KB) </p>

<p>http://hitswdb.googlepages.com/test.zip or http://hitswdatabase.googlecode.com/files/test.zip (Size: 940 KB) </p>

<p>  </p>

<p>Note: The gray-scale version of the database is also available upon request (Please contact hitswdb AT gmail.com).  </p>

<p>  </p>

<p>There&#39;s a new sheriff in town!Well, I wouldn&#39;t say sheriff so much as someone that doesn&#39;t want to see a project like this fall by the wayside.  We use it where I work and I&#39;ve offered to &quot;take over&quot; maintaining the code.  Does that mean there&#39;ll be a new version out?  Not anytime real soon.  In fact, I hate to admit that I haven&#39;t done much of anything with the code as of yet. </p>

<p>So, if you find bugs, have requests, have a question or just feel chatty, post away.  I&#39;ll do my best to answer any and all questions as quickly as possible. </p>

<p>I would like to thank Nate (and all the other contributers) for the tremendous amount of work he has done on libstats.  I can&#39;t speak for him directly, but I&#39;m willing to bet he&#39;s lurking in the shadows listening in should there be any questions that I am unable to answer. </p>

<p>Thanks in advance for your patience and understanding as I come up to speed on all things libstats. </p>

<p>--mark aka server.goon(at)gmail.com </p>

<p>Nate&#39;s farewellHi all, </p>

<p>After four years of development, I&#39;m leaving my current job and leaving this project an orphan. I&#39;d love for someone else to take up the mantle and make the project great -- or at least keep it from succumbing to bit rot. If you&#39;d like to be maintainer of a small, fairly simple open-source project, head to our discussion group and get in touch. </p>

<p>Thanks to all who have used libstats and helped to make it better. </p>

<p>Cheers! -Nate</p>

 title : The lingoblog Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>The main driving force behind Lingoblog is to provide a blogging engine that supports groups who want to communicate in multiple languages. I&#39;d like the engine to be as easy to set up as possible. Currently its extremely lightweight as there are only a few files in here ;-) It&#39;s still in the very early stages of development. I literally started it 4 hours before writing this at 4.00pm Sunday 3rd February 2008. </p>

<p>Rough and ready roadmap: </p>

<p>1) Homebrewed PHP framework that does not use the MVC pattern. </p>

<p>2) Automatic language detection. </p>

<p>3) Web interface for blogging / uploads. </p>

<p>4) Translation of blog articles into multiple languages by group members. </p>

<p>5) Support for images and custom formatting. </p>

<p>6) Switchable themes and styles. </p>

<p>7) Other stuff as and when I think of it. </p>

<p>Whether or not to use a framework :-/ </p>

<p>I&#39;ve started to go off some of the existing Web 2.0 frameworks - especially PHP ones. I&#39;ve decided to make my own framework for this project. My challenge is to &#39;NOT&#39; use the MVC pattern. Otherwise I would use an existing framework right ;-) The MVC pattern was invented in 79 and I&#39;d like to finally get away from Afro&#39;s, flared trousers and sugariness as we approach the end of the naughties! The framework I&#39;m thinking about will be easier to understand, develop in and will be a lot more flexible than the majority of frameworks out there. Ok lets get to work ;-)</p>

 title : The mysql-copy-database Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>SummaryA python script used to copy a MySQL database (including all relevant privileges) from one host to another, used as a wrapper around mysql and mysqldump. </p>

<p>For a full run down of usage instructions and options, run: mysql_copy_database -h </p>

<p>To test the script without making any changes, run: mysql_copy_database --dry-run </p>

<p>The script works roughly as follows: </p>

<p>You&#39;ll be prompted for source/destination host information, and the name of the DB to copy mysqldump will be used to dump the database to a temporary file The dumped database is re-created on the destination host The script will search for grants that appear relevant to the database on the source host You&#39;ll be prompted to apply each grant to the destination host </p>

<p>And that&#39;s it! </p>

<p>It&#39;s currently been tested on various linux and solaris systems, with MySQL versions 4 and 5. </p>

<p>To change any of the basic configuration settings, just edit them within the Settings class at the top of the file.  All options should be documented within it. </p>

<p>Any comments/suggestions/feature requests are more than welcome. </p>

<p>RequirementsSoftwareMySQL client The script uses the mysql and mysqldump binaries, and looks for them in /usr/bin unless an alternative location is specified in the script&#39;s settings. </p>

<p>Python ModulesThe follow python modules are used by the script: </p>

<p>MySQLdb pexpect</p>
 title : The n-cat Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>N-CATNumismatic Database Management for the Historian and Collector. </p>

<p>The software is build with embedded Firebird (Interbase) database engine and Qt C++ framework. </p>

<p>Update to the newest version  - view update instructions below. </p>

<p>Support most of NUDS fields (Numismatic Database Standard for column-oriented numismatic data sets) and additionally not limited number of images, documents and references per item. Designed for work with huge data sets. </p>

<p>Powerful and reliable embedded database engine. Easy backup and restore. Independent format. Relational database design. Not limited number of images, references, etc. per item. Build-in image viewer with rotation and scale support. Import from and export to Microsoft XML Speadsheet format, supported by Excel and OpenOffice. Run SQL query. Browse external databases, save data in Microsoft XML Spreadsheet file. Unicode support. Unicode character browser/input. Multiplatform. Runs on Linux and Windows (and also MacOS, but MacOS is not yet tested). And many more features... Installation Use local drive for installation. The embedded database should not be placed on network drive. Use NTFS file system if possible.  Choose installer or zip archive. If archive is taken - unpack it, open &quot;N-CAT&quot; directory and double-click at &quot;ncat.exe&quot; to start the application. Note: the installer and the application does not write anything into windows system directories and does not open any TCP ports - the embedded database works over local access. Update To update existing 1.x.x.x installation: download latest &quot;win32 update&quot; from &quot;Downloads&quot; section. Put the zip file into your N-CAT installation directory. Extract files (&quot;Extract here&quot;), confirm overwriting. You can also run installer and install over existing N-CAT 1.X.X installation, but be careful - don&#39;t overwrite your build-in database file (&quot;COLL0.FDB&quot;), the installer will ask about. Update to the newest version is recommended. Quick StartConnection dialog appears at application start-up. Click &quot;OK&quot; to connect to build-in embedded database. The database schema is divided into several collections. First collection, opened by default, may contain several demo entries. Documentation is in not yet released. Tip - try RIGHT-MOUSE-CLICK to access menus. Note: on Windows platform only one process can access the database file, you can not start multiple instances of N-CAT (or any other Firebird utilities) connected to the same database - connection will not succeed. Linux has little different architecture of embedded database server and you can start multiple instances of N-CAT connected safely to the same database, but it is not really useful for particular software. </p>

<p>Backup and restore </p>

<p> Backup and restore are essential for successful management of data sets. Backup and restore also rebuild indexes and shrink size of the database, giving back space of deleted items and improved indexes. Backup file has smaller size as database file and can be additionally compressed. Try backup and restore before you start creation of important data sets. </p>

<p>Images </p>

<p> Image can be stored as binary object inside the database (&quot;BLOB&quot; option), as link to the image file on local filesystem (&quot;LINK&quot; option) or as http link (&quot;URL&quot; option). &quot;Link&quot; and &quot;URL&quot; options do not store or modify image data, only reference is stored in the database. Selected images of obverse, reverse and edge can be set for item preview. Images can be viewed with build-in image viewer, copied to clipboard and saved (format, size and compression are adjustable). </p>

<p>Import existing column-orientated data sets from Excel </p>

<p> Open your Excel or OpenOffice Spredsheet file. One worksheet can be  imported at once. Save the whole file or selected worksheet as Microsoft XML Speadsheet file (again - XML file, not usual Excel XLS file).  Start N-CAT. Connect to database. Go to &quot;Collection&quot;-&gt;&quot;Import Data&quot;-&gt;&quot;Import from MS XML Spreadsheet&quot;. Select newly created Microsoft XML Speadsheet file, worksheet and destination collection. Table view with the data will appear - MAP THE COLUMNS double-clicking at the first (dark blue) row of the table view. Note: Fields marked yellow require special format, like integer or floating point, use reserved field if your data format doesn&#39;t match! &quot;Description&quot;, marked blue, can be used MULTIPLE times, the data will be applied to item&#39;s description. </p>

<p>More databases </p>

<p>The software is not limited by one build-in database. It is possible to create more databases over backup/restore procedure. Documentation follows. Note: one database contains many collections and can take huge data sets, creating of additional databases is optional. It is also possible - having some Firebird/Interbase knowledge - to set up an independent Firebird server installation, create database from N-CAT backup file and access it with N-CAT as client over network. </p>

<p>Contact: write to project owner (look at the current page) &quot;at googlemail.com&quot;. Feedback is welcome!</p>

 title : The openavanti Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>OpenAvanti: PHP Application FrameworkOpenAvanti is an object-oriented application framework written for PHP 5.3+, with support for PDO databases (PostgreSQL, MySQL and sqlite). This framework aims to simplify your application development process by providing you with a skeleton to immediately begin writing code without having to worry about the architectural details. </p>

<p>What Does it Offer?OpenAvanti offers the following features: </p>

<p>MVC Architecture Clean URL routing CRUD Automation Support for the most popular database engines Easy Validation Libraries for image, string, file and XML manipulation How is it Different than Other Frameworks?Unlike other, all encompassing frameworks, OpenAvanti does not force you into one method of application development, but instead provides you a set of tools to aid in developing applications the way you want to. If you don&#39;t like how something is laid out in OpenAvanti you don&#39;t have to use it, but the other tools are still available to you. </p>

 title : The sptrwt Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>The SPT Relational Database Web Tool (RWT) is a simple application that can help developers connect to databases configured as a DataSource in the application server or directly through JDBC. The RWT application attempts to replicate basic features found in the popular Aqua Data Studio application. Per user settings (saved connection parameters, saved queries), single and batch query processing, a history browser, multiple query browsers, a tree view of database metadata, and other features are supported.  Please read the manual for full details about the application, including simple use cases, features, installation instructions, etc.  You can view screen captures of the application under Downloads.  Source code for the application is available in subversion. </p>

<p>FeaturesThe following are the basic features provided by the tool: </p>

<p>Connect to databases configured in application server as DataSources. Configured DataSources are displayed in the application menu. Display a Connection dialogue through which users may specify the parameters for directly connecting to a database through JDBC. The connection parameters may be saved in which case the Connection will be added to the application menu of available databases. Display in a Tree the following types of database objects available in the connected database.  The schemas accessible to the user.  The tables available under a schema.  The views available under a schema.  The procedures and functions available under a schema.  The triggers defined in a schema.  The constraints (primary and foreign keys) defined in a schema. A query exeecution tool launched through a menu (multiple windows are supported). The query tool makes the following features available:  A free text area in which the user enters the query they wish to execute.  An optional text field which can be used to limit the maximum number of matching records fetched from the database.  A “Save” button that can be used to save the current query for easy access via a menu in the future.  The results of the query are displayed in tabular format. The results are pageable for convenience.  The results of the query can be exported to Excel through a “Export to Excel” button. Databases TestedPostgreSQL 8.2 Oracle 10.2.0.2.0 MySQL 5.0.41 Sybase 12.50 MS SQL Server 9.00.3077 DB2 Express-C - Works only partially.  DB2 JDBC driver does not allow scrollable cursors when tables contain LOB/XML types. PostgreSQL JDBC driver and the JTDS driver for Sybase and MS SQL Server are included with the downloaded package (and in subversion).  Other drivers are not included due to licencing restrictions (we could include the Oracle driver, but have no means of controlling downloads from export restricted countries).</p>
 title : The squirtle Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Welcome to SquirtleThe purpose of this little doodad is to help you prove to your employer, your client, your best friend, your dog, or God that NTLM is truly dead. It does this by taking control of any browser that comes into contact with it and making it perform NTLM authentication at will. By using a set of API calls you can embed Squirtle into existing penetration toolkits, proxies or other fun tools at your disposal. </p>

<p>The latest version of Squirtle should always be obtained with your SVN client of choice: </p>

<p>svn checkout http://squirtle.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/ squirtle-read-only </p>

<p>Squirtle Attack ScenariosXSS == Domination </p>

<p>Thanks to Internet Explorer&#39;s automatic security zones, servers on the &#39;inside&#39; are typically within the &quot;Trusted Zone&quot; by default. This means IE will negotiate and send NTLM credentials at the drop of a hat. With one cross site scripting vulnerability or even basic social engineering it&#39;s possible to now grab these hashes with a static nonce like crazy. Sure it&#39;s been done via SMB but this is HTTP! </p>

<p>More background here: http://grutz.jingojango.net/exploits/pokehashball.html -- Squirtle performs this attack by default when a user connects to it. </p>

<p>Pass The Dutchie </p>

<p>You&#39;ve heard of &quot;Pass The Hash&quot; and SMBRelay attacks where the attacker uses the LM/NT hashes to connect to SMB shares, right? Here&#39;s a new attack I&#39;m calling &quot;Pass The Dutchie&quot;. </p>

<p>Past attack methods have been focused on single-threaded attacks, either against a single server/resource or back to the client connecting. With Squirtle a client browser is held and asked to perform NTLM authentication at any time opening attacked resources to be any number of web servers, SMB shares, SQL Servers, etc.</p>

 title : The unihan-sqlite-3-database Open Source Project on Open Hub

 title : The allan Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>What is it about?As a programmer, you know the problem: you are good in one programming language, but you will or you are forced to do programming works in another language. The paradigm is the same, you may say. Yes, but every languages has it&#39;s own specific syntax and different level of abstraction. It will take an experienced programmer days or even weeks to be able to work with a new language. Even so, you need to look up in reference books about certain syntax, like What does the class declaration in C++ looks like? </p>

<p>A Paradigm driven online ReferenceALLAN is the acronym of All Languages. With the project ALLAN, we are aiming at a paradigm driven online reference for all programming languages. The user just need to input a keyword, then he will get articles for languages he selected. With ALLAN, you never need to look up in thick reference books, and as ALLAN will use a wiki-engine, you get the opportunity to edit the items or add new items. </p>

 title : The babel-parse Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Babel is almost like a programming language, except it does not impose any compile time or runtime semantics on the code it parses. It parses the code, generates a syntax tree, and provides some tools to help the developer produce more fine grained parsing, via a breadth first tree walking algorithm, as well as composing multiple such iterative treewalking parsers together in order to encapsulate different aspects of a final programming language. It also intends to provide a stack based &#39;forth&#39; like reverse polish intermediate code specification, as well a several backends to assist in final execution, or compilation of the intermediate language. </p>

<p>This project is, at the moment, being developed in the haskell programming language. All of the libraries are haskell libraries. </p>

<p>Babel&#39;s source tree is not maintained here on google. Instead, it is maintained in a darcs repository here. There will be snapshots and binary packages submitted to the download section on this project page, once they become available.</p>

 title : The booleannet Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Boolean Network ModelingThe goal of this software package is to provide intuitive and accessible tools for simulating biological regulatory networks in a boolean formalism. Using this simulator biologist and bioinformaticians can specify their system in a simple textual language then explore various dynamic behaviors via a web interface or an application programming interface (API) each designed to facilitate scientific discovery, data collection and reporting. </p>

<p>The software is primarly distributed as Python source code and requires that Python 2.5 (or later) be installed on the target computer.  </p>

<p>Bugfix NoteJanuary 7, 2010. Please note that versions 1.2.0 to 1.2.4 of the BooleanNet package have  a bug that cause the node updates to execute in original (listed) order during the first iteration, before randomizing the order of nodes for subsequent iterations. This bug affects only the asynchronous update mechanism.  </p>

<p>The net effect of the bug is that for certain type of rules the first execution of them may funnel the states into the basin of one of the attractors. Overall the answers will not be incorrect but, depending on the rules and order of nodes they may be incomplete. Please update to the latest version. My apologies. Istvan Albert </p>

<p>PublicationBoolean network simulations for life scientist by István Albert, Juilee Thakar, Song Li, Ranran Zhang, and Réka Albert in Source Code for Biology and Medicine (2008)  </p>

<p>IntroductionWhen trying to understand the role and functioning of a regulatory network, the first step is to assemble the components of the network and the interactions between them. The experimental advances in the large scale mapping of regulatory networks are fairly recent, but modeling efforts date back to the end of 1960s thanks to the pioneering work of Stuart Kauffman and Rene Thomas. </p>

<p>In a Boolean representation we assume that nodes are equivalent, and their interactions form a directed graph in which each node receives inputs from its neighbors (nodes that are connected to it). The state of nodes is described by binary (ON/OFF) variables, and the dynamic behavior of each variable, that is, whether it will be ON or OFF at next moment, is governed by a Boolean function. In general, a Boolean or logical function is written as a statement acting on the inputs using the logical operators and, or and not and its output is ON(OFF) if the statement is true (false). </p>

<p>DocumentationA detailed documentation is available on our external website. This documentation is also included in the source code distribution. See the: </p>

<p>Installation  Tutorials  for a quick overview on how the make the library work for you.  </p>

<p>About the libraryNote as of version 1.2 (Nov 12, 2008) the library has acquired several new features (see below) and underwent a substantial reorganization. To keep old code from interfering with new one the library namespace has been changed to boolean2 </p>

<p>In this software package, we implement mutliple advanced methodologies which combine discrete logical rules with more realistic assumptions regarding the relative timescales of the  processes: </p>

<p>synchronous updates are performed in listed order, but the states change only at the end of the update round asynchronous updates are performed in random order and the states immediately reflect the changes, this makes the model stochastic.  ranked asynchronous updates are performed in rank order, within the same rank the updates take place asynchronously time synchronous update are performed in time. Each rule has a time delay associated with them, updates take place at multiples of these delays piece wise differential updates associate a set of continuous variables (concentrations, decay rates and thresholds) to each discrete variable in the system. The dynamics of these continuous variables is determined by a linear system of piecewise differential equations, leading to a hybrid model in the manner first suggested by Leon Glass and collaborators.  </p>

<p>Example RulesHere are a few example rules for BooleanNet covering various research projects. Most of these rules were collected via a thorough literature search and were manually curated into their final form. These rules are available in the examples/samples directory of the source code distribution. </p>

<p>Rules for abscicis acid induced stomatal closure in plants  aba.txt published as Song Li, Sarah Assmann and Réka Albert Predicting essential components of signal transduction networks: dynamic model of guard cell abscisic acid signaling PLoS Biology 4 (10): e312, 2006   </p>

<p>Rules for T-cell large granular lymphocyte leukemia simulation  LGL.txt published as Ranran Zhang, Mithun Vinod Shah, Jun Yang, Susan B. Nyland, Xin Liu, Jong K. Yun, Réka Albert, and Thomas P. Loughran, Jr. Network Model of Survival Signaling in LGL Leukemia PNAS, 2008 (to appear) </p>

<p>Rules for mammalian immune response to B. bronchiseptica infection  immune.txt published as J. Thakar, M. Pilione, G. Kirimanjeswara, E. Harvill and R. Albert Modeling Systems-Level Regulation of Host Immune Responses PLoS Computational Biology 6, e109 (2007   Some of the resulting plots based on the rules above: </p>

<p>  </p>

<p>CreditsThe library has been designed and implemented by István Albert using previous work, ideas and contributions from: </p>

<p>Song Li Juilee Thakar Ranran Zhang Assieh Saadatpour Moghaddam  None of us would be thinking about Boolean Networks if it weren&#39;t for Réka Albert. </p>

<p>Our software relies on the following third party libraries that are distributed with  the software: </p>

<p>PLY by David Beazley The following library must be also installed if the engine will be used in plde mode (piece-wise linear differential equations): </p>

<p>matplotlib by Dave Hunter</p>

 title : The buddyfusion Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Problem StatementAs theory and practice shows social networks ought to get a more and more important impact for the life of modern people. An unmeasurable amount of social networks exists within the World Wide Web, each one with its own social purpose, its advantages or disadvantages and it’s very special focus concerning aim and target group.  Deduced from all these networks people get not only confused by the variety but also overstrained by maintaining all their personal profiles. Besides it’s not always obvious, what network to use for a certain service; user initiated tasks (messages, blogs) are not available from each network, often services are liable to pay costs. Furthermore this effect results in multiple definitions of friendships with the same person in different networks without having any relation or correlation between them. Another issue of current social network is the representation of social relationships between persons. Not only that most of the networks show lists of friends just in a tabular format without visual intuitive acquisition, also translative relations aren’t visualized in a clear and reproducible way. </p>

<p>ApproachThe aim of this exercise is to develop an application to visualize social relationships of persons among various platforms. Persons are represented as nodes and connections between those nodes give information about their relationships. Furthermore the presence of a certain person within diverse networks shall be displayed and made clearly arranged. To support various platforms the intended application is based on a multi layer visualization, wherein the user should be even able to aggregate one person’s accounts among several platforms to define one physical person out of it. </p>

<p>ImplementationThe implementation of the application is ought to be based on the Java Programming Language. For the visual representation the visualization toolkit Prefuse (www.prefuse.org) will be used. As Java Applications are usually not able to be executed over the Web, additional technology is necessary. Webstart http://java.sun.com/j2se/1.5.0/docs/guide/javaws not only allows us to execute an usual Java Desktop Application over the Http Protocol but also supports features like incremental updates and downloads. For testing our application we will create XML based data (dummy data) of persons with relationships from various platforms. </p>

<p>Graphical VisualizationThe following figures show the future functionality of the planned prototype. Figure 1 exemplifies the basic visualization of the different social network platform after the import of the XML (dummy) data. This visualization is ego-centered and the persons connected appear within their social network platforms. Obviously people appearing in different networks are displayed as doubles. The graph is network centered.   </p>

<p>Basic Network Centered View </p>

<p>After the import the prototype shall be able to suggest the merger of possible identical persons, as shown in next paragraph.   </p>

<p>Suggested Merger of Doubles </p>

<p>As a result of this suggestion the graph shows the social network of the user in a different and partly simplified way (next figure). Information on the social network platforms a certain person utilizes is visualized via multiple connections to one merged node.   </p>

<p>Partly Simplified Graph </p>

<p>According to the knowledge of the user of his personal network it shall be possible to merge all identical persons. Figure 4 presents the result of a manual merger of all identical persons. The focus of the graph is now adjusted to a more person centered view instead of a network centered view.   </p>

<p>Resulting Person Centered View</p>
 title : The ccnitdgp Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>An online judge is an online system to test programs in programming contests. They are also used to practice for such contests. The system can compile and execute your code, and test your code with pre-constructed data. Submitted code may be run with restrictions, including time limit, memory limit, security restriction and so on. The output of the code will be captured by the system, and compared with the standard output. The system will then return the result.  This judge runs on Linux machines.  The main drive and motivation behind this project is to inculcate the culture of programming among students, helping them understand the importance of algorithms as a problem solving tool, and making them recognise the power of Linux as a powerful programming platform. The judge is built using opensource technologies and tools. Currently, it judges programs written in C/C++ only, but support for other languages may be added very easily. </p>

<p>When this project was undertaken by us, its aim was to extract the programming talent hidden in our college students by organising an intra-lan programming contest every week. The Linux Users&#39; Group wanted to be active all the year round. With its active support, its first run itself was successful with 1100 submissions in a span of 10 hours. Having tested the software on our college lan 7-8 times, it was decided that CodeCracker would host a national level online programming contest during MUKTI ,NIT Durgapur&#39;s national level tech fest on free and open source software, on 4th and 5th January. In colleges a common problem is that though there are good programmers, they are hesitant to contribute to the opensource movement. Through this software we encouraged our friends to use GCC as the standard compiler, and we distributed several versions of Linux on our lan in the course. There was a phenomenal rise in the number of Linux users since then and people took to programming actively. Having found some of the best coders in our college through CodeCracker, we now plan to found the Software Development Unit(LUG SDU), a new arm of LUG comprising of members selected from the winners of CodeCracker events held in the college. This unit will be involved actively in developing and contributing to opensource projects.</p>

 title : The coglang Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Cog is a language designed around the new programming paradigm  &quot;cognitive programming&quot;. Cognitive programming is programming by specifications rather than having to spell out algorithms in full as is necessary in most languages. Cog has a knowledge base of programming techniques which it uses to translate specifications into code.</p>

<p>Cog uses AI-style inductive reasoning processes to infer from its knowledge base how to best create a program. The knowledge base contains a wide collection of programming techniques and is intended to be grown as a community collaborative project.</p>
 title : The cologo Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Cologo is collaborative web-based programming environment.  Cologo&#39;s most likely uses are education and experimentation, but its features are amenable to a variety of uses. </p>

<p>Cologo programs are written in Google Spreadsheets, and multiple people can collaborate over the web to write and edit code and documentation.  A spreadsheet can include procedure definitions, comments, formatted text, and data used by the program, all in one sheet.  Users can collaborate on data sets as well as programs. </p>

<p>The runtime environment is a Gadget, configured to use a spreadsheet-like data source for the program code.  The gadget is typically inserted onto the Google Spreadsheet containing the program, but it can also be added to a iGoogle page, any web page, or any compatible gadget container.  The Gadget can use any data source compatible with the Google Visualizations API.  Google Spreadsheets provides collaborative editing, and updates the gadget with changes in real-time. </p>

<p>The programming language is a faithful variant of Logo, including turtle graphics.  Cologo uses slightly different syntax than traditional Logo to make the best use of the spreadsheet layout for programs.  The Cologo interpreter can be paused and resumed for inspection of variables and debugging. </p>

<p>The Cologo engine is implemented entirely in web browser JavaScript, using the Gadget and Google Visualization APIs.  The turtle graphics system uses the HTML 5 canvas feature supported by Firefox, Safari, and Opera, and works with Internet Explorer using an HTML canvas plugin.  Cologo can be used in a browser without canvas support with the turtle features disabled. </p>

<p>This Google Code project is for the development of the Cologo runtime environment, gadget and language.  For more information on using Cologo, visit the Cologo website: http://www.cologo-lang.org/</p>
 title : The comp-lang-polyglot Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>The Polyglot Programming Project gathers specifications for short scripts (programs), which are then written in multiple programming languages such as java, perl, php, python, rebol, ruby, etc. </p>

<p>Each script (or program) is a short recipe, phrase, or set of phrases. Scripts are normally less than 10 lines of code. Scripts are almost always less than 48 lines of code. However, the goal is to write the same script (matching the same specification) in all languages. </p>

<p>The goal is provide hundreds (maybe even thousands) of short specifications (program function descriptions), and then write a script that performs the function, and translations of that same script into every other popular language. </p>

<p>So it&#39;s the same concept as saying: </p>

<p>print &quot;Hello, world!&quot;   </p>

<p>in many computer languages, however,with the goal of translating many other phrases. </p>

<p>In many ways, we are similar to the PLEAC project (which is translating the Perl Cookbook into many other computer languages) --but we are focused on shorter recipes and phrases.</p>

 title : The coord Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>CoordIntroductionWhat is Coord? Quick Start How to Install How to Program Support for Other Programming Languages - java, python, php, and etc. FAQ Coord TutorialCoord Tutorial - coord tutorial (remark: see it after downloading) Demos in Coord Tutorial HOWTO Coord - Introduce how to work with Coord HOWTO Coord in Java - Introduce how to work with Coord in Java HOWTO Coord in Python - Introduce how to work with Coord in Python HOWTO Coord in PHP - Introduce how to work with Coord in PHP HOWTO Coord !MapReduce - Introduce how to perform MapReduce using Coord Data Analyses TutorialNCDC Dataset A legacy code to crawl NCDC dataset - To explain how to thrust a legacy code into a distributed environment without many modifications, first we need to know how the legacy code works in a single computing environment. This tutorial shows a NCDC cralwer written in python, and later parallelizing it with Coord will be introduced in the other tutorial Parallelize NCDC dataset crawlers with Coord - To crawl NCDC dataset, a legacy code in python was used in a single machine. However, the crawling consumes too many time, so the legacy code should be rewritten for multiple machines. Through Coord, it is not difficult to parallelize the lagacy code in a cluster computing environment. In this tutorial, I will show how to use Coord to process crawlers in parallel without many modifications NCDC dataset Analyses using Coord !MapReduce - Introduce how to perform MapReduce using Coord MovieLens Dataset Analyze !MovieLens dataset with Coord !MapReduce - Coord provides C++ MapReduce framework to analyze large-scale dataset. This tutorial shows how to use Coord to analyze MovieLens dataset Sample Dataset Large-scale Graph Search with Coord - Coord enables a large-scale graph search. In this tutorial, some simple triples can be tested in Coord to search some query patterns and find some hidden relations between subject-subject, subject-object, or object-object DownloadCoord 0.4.0 - provide a public tutorial for coord and dataset for testing Coord 0.3.5 - add a graph search module for enabling semantic search Coord 0.3.0 - provide C++ MapReduce framework   </p>

<p>DocumentsCoord Tutorial - public coord tutorial, presented at 2009 NHN DeView (remark: see it after downloading) Technical Report - written by Korean Language Introduction to Coord - This was internally presented in 2008 NHN DeView.  Getting InvolvedCoord is a new open source to dramatically integrate information technology into distributed computing environments. We encourage you to make full use of Coord and contribute your expertise. We need students, engineers, and researchers to participate in the development parts such as information retrieval, data/text mining, machine learning, semantic search, and etc. Join the mailing lists and participate in the discussions around the development of Coord.  title : The cppagent Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>This C++ class library provides a simple framework for developing soft real-time systems using an agent-based programming model.  The library is especially geared toward robotics applications. </p>

<p>The library incorporates ideas from flow-based programming, swarm AI, software componentry, and control theory. </p>

<p>In this context, an agent is a software component which: </p>

<p>processes and manipulates data streams, is autonomous, in that it requires no interaction from users or other agents, is entirely decoupled from other system components, has no interface (black-box view), operates in an independent thread of execution. </p>

<p>Data streams consist of well-defined datagrams which: </p>

<p>like UDP datagrams, are unreliable, unlike UDP datagrams, are ordered, unlike objects, are not explicitly bound to methods or events. </p>

<p>The agent-based programming model encourages engineers to design complex systems in terms of simple processing components (agents).  Agents are entirely unaware of other agents, making the agent-based model inherently component-based.  The server-client model is entirely dismissed, preventing any wait-for-response behavior.  In fact, since all inter-agent communication is unreliable, it is impractical to implement any hand shaking between agents.  This limitation encourages one-way data streams rather than two-way communication or RPC.</p>

 title : The daot Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>The Dao to programming: new generation programming languageIn the dao to programming, some new forms, such as 3(x+5)(4a(5b+A11)), where A11 means A1 in other programming, |x|, the absolute value of x, n!, the factorial of n, date and time format, file path, url, email address, a menu in the restaurant, and all that, would become legal source code.  title : The django-contract Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Programming by Contract for Django Pre-conditions  Post-conditions  Invariants  
<br/> Helps with testing!   Easier to find bugs!  django-contract is a django application providing Programming by Contract constraint checking in docstrings. The solution uses a modified version of contract.py by Terence Way. Originally presented for PEP 316 - Programming by Contract for Python. </p>

<p>Installation and configuration Examples and the Todo demo applicationSome examples of how you might use django contract Check out the example application for more details on how it all fits together Why should i use django contract?Makes it easy to add optional constraints on methods. You can run the development sever with a hardened environment, without additional performance penalty when deployed. Things like forms and input validation gets another level of checking while developing your apps. Code coverage is greatly increased when combined with traditional testing. Works with both unittests and doctests. (coverage with django-contract) NOT just for formal verification, formal specification and Hoare logic. Example workflow: </p>

<p>You define a Model with title = models.CharField(max_length=200) You come to think of that only whitespaces titles should not be allowed, so you define an invariant for the model: len(self.title.strip()) &gt; 0 Continue with the rest of the model definitions... You finally make the views and forms for submitting entries. First round of testing and everything seems to work, the title is not set to blank=True so the field is required. Step two is where you usually try to make a note to remember to check this in the form. Now you can write down a check right there while defining the models.  </p>

<p>While testing if someone tries to submit an entry with a title consisting of just some spaces its not just silently accepted. The InvariantViolationError is raised by all model methods trying to operate on a model with a whitespace title.    </p>

<p>Programming by Contract for PythonThe modified contract.py is included in this project mainly because modifications made are aimed at getting it to work together with django not patching contract.py per se. There is some really funky meta-programming/monkey-patching going on in contract.py, we gave up trying to understand the inner workings and settled on just making it work with django. </p>

<p>Details on modifications to contract.py and its usage About django-contract</p>

<p>  This project is developed as a part of a research project at the Department of Information Technologies at Åbo Akademi University</p>

 title : The eiffel-state Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>EiffelState is a library and a visual editor supporting Automata-based programming in Eiffel programming language and EiffelStudio IDE. </p>

<p>The main ideas behind the project are the following: </p>

<p>The central notion of Object-oriented Automata-based programming is the automated class. Unlike a regular class in OOP the automated class is a model of an object with complex (or state-dependent) behavior. At each point such an object can be in one of the relatively small set of control states. Depending on the current control state the object can react differently to the same input. The logic of its behavior (the dependency between the control states and reactions, as well as transitions between control states) are captured in object&#39;s controller, which is essentially a finite automaton. To its clients an automated class looks just like any normal class. Inside it consists of a controller (responsible for behavior logic) and a control object, which is a regular class, responsible for behavior semantics.  One of the most convenient and vivid ways to describe automata is using State-Transition Diagrams (STD) - graphs that have control states as vertices and transitions as edges. Each transition can have a condition and an action. Condition may involve events (that correspond to feature names in O-O world) and queries on control object. Actions may involve commands to the control object. Some people hate visual software construction, thus we are providing a library that allows one to describe automated classes in Eiffel as directly as possible. We also provide a visual editor that allows one to view controllers of automated objects as STD and also construct and edit them visually. The Eiffel code generated from an STD will use the library mentioned above, and thus will be high-level and human readable. This should support transparency between two different views of the controller: the textual one and the graphical one, allowing the developer to switch from one to another at any point. </p>

<p>Presentation on Automata-based programming: pptx/pdf</p>

 title : The fdjs Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>FDJS is a simple libary that empowers javascript coders to work with a functional, declarative programming paradigm. </p>

<p>Here&#39;s a running example: http://fdjs.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/fdjs_ex1.htm </p>

<p>Remember the last time you were debugging a program and asked &quot;how did this variable ever get set to that value?&quot;  You were probably dealing with a path dependency--some series of steps occurred in an unexpected order and produced an unanticipated result.  Such problems are typical in the procedural, imperative programming paradigm we use in most programming languages. </p>

<p>Now imagine asking the same question of a cell on a spreadsheet.  If just one cell is showing an incorrect value, you need to look no further than the underlying formula which defines its value.  The cause and effect are closely coupled.  Moreover, the cell is internally consistent--only the formula can make the value &quot;right&quot; or &quot;wrong&quot;, and it is path independent.  These two features describe the normal expectations of a functional, declarative programming paradigm. </p>

<p>It is possible to use functional, declarative programming practices even in some languages that are typically procedural and imperative, including Javascript. </p>

<p>FDJS demonstrates how Javascript user interface development can benefit from the functional declartive paradigm. </p>

<p>Join the group http://groups.google.com/group/fdjs-discuss if you are interested in FDJS, and let me know you&#39;re trying it out.</p>

 title : The fizz-buzz Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>What is FizzBuzz?The first reference on the web I found to the &quot;FizzBuzz Question&quot; was in a Coding Horror blog post back on February 26, 2007. Although the author is quoting another blog post, this is where I first heard of the &quot;FizzBuzz Problem&quot;. FizzBuzz is a litmus test during interviews for software developers which essentially tries to answer the question, &quot;Can you write any software at all?&quot; with an extremely simple problem, stated as: </p>

<p>Write a program that prints the numbers from 1 to 100. But for multiples of three print &quot;Fizz&quot; instead of the number and for the multiples of five print &quot;Buzz&quot;. For numbers which are multiples of both three and five print &quot;FizzBuzz&quot;. 
<br/>So, this is a project with FizzBuzz samples?No. This &#39;project&#39; contains all the work I do for various personal projects. I needed a free wiki and source code repository, so here I am. I&#39;m calling this fizz-buzz because I anticipate putting more than 10 years of code up here eventually. So, it kind of feels like a programmer litmus test of sorts. </p>

 title : The functional-actionscript Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>A simple library to encourage functional style programming methods in actionscript 3.0 and above. </p>

<p>Have added the &#39;Functional&#39; class that adds methods to the Object class. This makes it a little easier to start exploring functional style programming. </p>

<p>Getting StartedYou start by adding the following 2 lines to your Flex code in an an initialisation section. </p>

<p>import handy.Functional;
<br/>...
<br/>Functional.MakeSystemFunctional();Some simple examplesvar a:* = [1,23,1,&quot;beef&quot;,2,17,100];    //set up an Array
<br/>var b:Object = a.Select( function(i:Object):Boolean { return i &lt; 70 } );    //b is actually an Array
<br/>trace( b );    // b should contain [1,23,1,2,17] -- notice that the String is ignored</p>

<p>var c:Object = a.Reject( function(i:Object):Boolean { return i == 1 } );
<br/>trace( c );    // c should contain [23,&quot;beef&quot;,2,17,100]</p>

<p>a = [
<br/>  {a:1, b:11},
<br/>  {a:2, b:22},
<br/>  {a:3, b:33},
<br/>  {a:4, b:44},
<br/>  {a:5, b:55}
<br/>];
<br/>b = a.Find( function(i:Object):Boolean { return i.b == 44 } );
<br/>trace( b ); // b should be the object {a:4, b:44}This makes Searching and manipulating collections of Objects much easier/readable!</p>

 title : The ESMS Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Electronic Soccer Management Simulator, </p>
 summary : <p>GenetiK (Genetic Kernel)GenetiK is a generic framework that supports evolutionary algorithms. </p>

<p>According to the evolutionary approach, solutions to particular problems can be represented as individuals of a population. For each individual, a particular function, called &#39;&#39;fitness&#39;&#39;, can be defined to associate a high fitness scores with &#39;good&#39; solutions. </p>

<p>Starting from any set of individuals, evolving this population (with a process that loosely resembles darwinian selection in biology) results, after a sufficient number of &#39;&#39;generations&#39;&#39;, in a new population of high-fitness individuals. In other words, starting from any set (even randomly generated) of potential solutions to a problem, it is possible to obtain new sets of progressively &#39;better&#39; solutions, eventually resulting in the selection of an optimal (or near-optimal) solution. </p>

<p>Therefore, depending on the nature of the problem to be solved, it is possible to find a good solution by expressing candidate solutions and their fitness in an appropriate way. Even adopting the same evolutionary algorithm, but two different representations of individuals and fitness, can lead to dramatically different results, therefore finding a good representation of individuals and their fitness is crucial to the success or failure of a particular application. </p>

<p>The idea behind the GenetiK project is to let users experiment with evolutionary computation without having to code from scratch the algorithm that deals with the evolution itself, but rather let them concentrate on their specific tasks and objectives. This allows users to focus on finding good representations for candidate solution, the best ways to measure fitness and other aspects, but, at the same time, allowing them to fine-tune the algorithm to their specific needs by customizing its behaviour, if required. </p>

<p>Project StructureThe GenetiK framework is divided in 5 subprojects: </p>

<p>genetiK -- that includes the common base classes genetiK::ga -- specialized in dealing with Genetic Algorithms genetiK::gp -- oriented towards Genetic Programming genetiK::gp::st -- dedicated to Strongly Typed Genetic Programming genetiK::util -- includes all the utility classes </p>

<p>Here you can find an UML diagram describing the structure of the framework. (Source XMI file, generated with Umbrello) </p>

<p> </p>

<p>genetiK provides the common evolutionary algorithms functionalities, while genetiK::ga, genetiK::gp and genetiK::gp::st contains the specific classes that should be extended to develop a specific solution. You can consult the annotated example (the genetic algorithm that comes with the library) to see how the framework can be used. </p>

<p>DocumentationPlease refer to HTML documentation for more information. </p>

<p>Getting the codeTo check out the current version of GenetiK use </p>

<p>svn checkout http://genetik.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/ genetikand compile with </p>

<p>make(We hope that your current platform is supported  ) </p>

<p>Running the exampleAfter compiling the library, you can run the example by typing </p>

<p>./bin/example</p>

 title : The humbug Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>humbug is an esoteric programming language. Like other esoteric programming languages it eschews the bonds of user-friendliness to achieve the ultimate goal of a programming language - to be so obscure and mind-twisting that it&#39;s almost impossible to program in.</p>

<p>humbug&#39;s special feature is that it is programmed entirely in bugs - ie. the code itself has no meaning, only the bugs have meaning. So you program by using clever combinations of bugs. It&#39;s all a bit of fun.</p>

<p>humbug is the first programming language where the bugs in your code are the fundamental sematic construct. The reasoning is: if it&#39;s so hard to write a program without bugs why not make the bugs be the program?</p>

<p>A humbug program looks like a poorly written C program. But this is misleading - the C semantics are totally ignored and all the meaning of the program comes from the placement and types of bugs within the code. A very skilled humbug programmer can create programs which look like valid C but in fact have many bugs and only work correctly when executed as humbug.</p>

<p>Some other famous esoteric programming languages include Intercal and Brainf**k, so if humbug sounds fun you may want to check them out.</p>

 title : The iconinterpreter Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Icon interpreter in JavaThis project contains an implementation of an interpreter for a small part of the Icon programming language and is the code product of a student project at the IT University of Copenhagen. The interpreter is written in Java 5.0 and may be studied and used in any way compliant with the GPL. The authors of the project suspects this may be of interest to other students interested in the implementation of programming languages. </p>

<p>Icon constructsThe implementation is focused on a specific method of modeling evaluation of a goal-directed language and thus only aims to support an illustrative amount of types and language constructs. Only the integer type is supported. This table shows how much of Icon is implemented in this version of the program: </p>

<p>+ -   Binary arithmetic operators.   -  Unary operator.   &lt; =  Binary (in)equality operators.   | &amp; ;  Connectives.   to  Integer generator (without step).   </p>

<p>About the implementationThe implementation is essentially a realization of the method illustrated in “Denotational semantics of a goal-directed language” (Gudeman, D.A, 1999, ACM Transactions on Programming Languages and Systems 14(1), 107–125). </p>

<p>The interpreter makes use of the explicit representation of several continuations to model the backtracking and goal-directed evaluation which is the most interesting feature of the Icon programming language. </p>

<p>As part of the distributed code a parser implemented in Coco/R serves to map the concrete syntax of Icon to the abstract syntax encoded in the supplied Java classes. </p>

<p>Build in an object-oriented style, this implementation may, with relative little effort, be extended to support a wider range of Icon features and constructs. </p>

<p>Anyone interested in Icon in Java should checkout Jcon, a complete Java-implementation of Icon. </p>

<p>Getting startedAs mentioned this will only be of interest to people who want to study the code. This is not user software. </p>

<p>To check out the code with subversion and build it with ant; open your terminal or prompt and paste the following: </p>

<p>svn checkout http://iconinterpreter.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/ iconinterpreter 
<br/>cd iconinterpreter 
<br/>antTo run the interpreter write: </p>

<p>java -cp out iconinterpreter/Icon</p>

 title : The jsnapp Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>jsnap is a standalone server that acts as a middleware between clients that want to execute SQL statements -yet not want to deal with database programming issues like pooling, timeouts, cursors etc.- and database servers. </p>

<p>If Java is installed, running jsnap is as easy as running the script sh-server. No other external dependencies, all needed jar&#39;s are in the lib/ folder. Development started with JDK 1.5 and is now continuing with 1.6. Though not tested, it probably would work perfectly with 1.4. </p>

<p>Features1) Server configuration is done via an XML file and configuration can be modified on the fly even when the server is up and running. Server&#39;s outputs are done via log4j, configure it anyway (console, file, smtp etc.) you like. </p>

<p>2) Server configuration mainly consists of listeners and databases; listeners listen to TCP/IP requests from clients and databases are the resources on which accepted client requests are executed. One of the configured databases is the internal database that is used by the jsnap server for user/group management, access control and logging. </p>

<p>3) Listeners may accept requests of different types. That is, the way a request is encoded and transported is totally parametric. Requests could be sent via HTTP to a listener that is accepting HTTP connections or they could be sent via a user-defined protocol/transport over plain/secure sockets. Requests could be sent over an SSL connection regardless of the way they are encoded. </p>

<p>A listener is configured to accept a certain type of request, e.g. HTTPRequest, SSLRequest, from a certain port. jsnap server may be configured to run as many listeners as desired. </p>

<p>4) Databases are basically connection pools. Pool and connection management (connect/disconnect/ping/reconnect...) is performed by jsnap and clients are totally isolated from these processes. A connection management policy for each database is easily set via the configuration file also; jsnap could take databases online/offline (in terms of client access) according to the defined policy and the status of the database. </p>

<p>All databases with JDBC drivers could be managed by jsnap; however, this is not a strict requirement. Although not currently in place, support for other data sources (spreadsheets, text files etc.) could very easily be implemented. Also the generic JDBC driver could be extended (specialized) in order to take advantage of some features of the original JDBC drivers, e.g. Oracle&#39;s ping, Postgres&#39; cancelQuery etc. </p>

<p>5) jsnap server allows a client to execute a SQL statement. Moreover, a client may also ask the server to execute a SQL statement but keep the resultset open until a commit/rollback or timeout. That is, for INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE statements, the client is able to delay the commit/rollback, disabling autocommit. This also means that, for the SELECT statements, the client may scroll over the query&#39;s output (if the database supports scrolling) or view only certain sections (in terms of row numbers) of the result set. </p>

<p>The server also allows the client to specify how the output of the executed SQL statement should be formatted. Currently, the client may receive outputs in CSV, HTML or XML format. Formatting is done transparently from the client; the only thing the client needs to do is to read from the socket. It is also very easy to implement a user-defined binary/ascii encoding for the result sets, allowing jsnap to work with, for example, Borland&#39;s datasets. </p>

<p>6) Java classes for Java clients are already in place. A Java client only needs to instantiate an object, fill in the SQL body, parameters, user credentials etc. and call send() to send the request; the call to receive() fetches all the requested data nicely formatted for processing. With jsnap, database access is equivalent to writing/reading from a socket. </p>

<p>Since database access is simplified to socket programming, it is possible to code in any programming language. For example, when coding with C it is easier to open a socket and write/read from it rather than working with low-level database libraries or precompilers. Even a web browser could be jsnap&#39;s client, an example SqlExecutor.html exists within the source. </p>

<p>7) jsnap allows setting an authentication policy and an access control policy for every database. jsnap server could allow/deny running a SQL statement according to the database&#39;s security policies. User based policies are implemented, group and IP address based policies are on the way, database object (e.g. tables, fields) based policies are planned. All access to databases are logged if required. </p>

<p>8) jsnap&#39;s web interface allows administrators and users to login for certain operations. Users, as expected, are only able to view limited features, whereas, administrators also perform user/group management and view statistics. </p>

<p>Ongoing1) FIRST AND FOREMOST: Documentation! (except inline.) </p>

<p>2) Several access control policies will be implemented. </p>

<p>3) Support for scheduling SQL statements will be implemented. </p>

<p>4) JDBC&#39;s timeout mechanism is not good enough; a better and generic timeout mechanism will be implemented. </p>

<p>5) Web interface will have more features. </p>

<p>6) Generic JDBC driver will be extended to take advantage of original JDBC drivers.</p>

 summary : <p>Online judge for programming contests.</p>

 summary : <p>What is KorusKorus is a very simple yet powerful parallel and distributed programming framework.  It aims to improve the performance and scalability of Java applications.  </p>

<p> </p>

<p>Why you should try Korus?1. Futuristic approach: Make your programs ready for the next generation multi-core hardware. </p>

<p>2. Inherent Concurrency: No need to understand thread-programming to use Korus. Korus provides thread-less concurrency by way of code-context-switching.  </p>

<p>3. Actor Pattern: Korus is based on Actor Design Pattern (characterized by inherent concurrency of computation within). One of first “pure” actor pattern frameworks in Java.  </p>

<p>4. Non Blocking concurrency, No thread synchronization, No Deadlock and Starvation </p>

<p>5. Very Simple: Korus is very simple to use, very simple to deploy (one single jar file), and very simple to understand. Try it out yourself here. </p>

<p> </p>

<p>Getting StartedGetting started with Korus is as fast as Korus itself.  </p>

<p>Download Sample.zip from here. Execute the file run.bat or run.sh depending on your OS </p>

<p>You can download the Korus from the download section. It consists of sample programs, Java docs and korus.jar file. </p>

<p>The best way to start is by having a look at the Getting started page. If you want to have a very quick feel go to the Getting Started Quickly section in guide. It will take only 5 minutes to run the sample program if you have a JDK environment.  </p>

<p> </p>

<p>Complete Guide to KorusIf you want to have a detailed understanding of Korus, please visit the Complete Details section. </p>

 title : The libiada Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>The classes library for analysis of large data arrays, based on new approach in the sphere of informatics - interval analyze.  </p>

<p>Interval analysis allows to describe a positional relationship of data arrays elements. The most frequent data arrays are discrete audio signals, linguistic and biological texts, images or any statistic data. </p>

<p>Traditionally, probabilistic approaches are used to research into such objects (data arrays). Except of Markovian chains and correlation dependences, which indirectly take account of positional relationship of data arrays elements, probabilistic approaches take account just only of the information about the quantitative composition of the data arrays. </p>

<p>Numerical characteristics, obtained with the help of interval analysis, can be used for solution of data mining (clustering, etc.) </p>

<p>That library will be developed basing on C#, adjusted for .NET technologies. This fact will allows to include that library in software developing basing on other programming languages. </p>

<p>Bibliography: 1. Gumenjuk A.S. - The calculation of the positional relationship of elements in data arrays (formal analysis of the structured data composition) // 9th International Conference SPEECH AND COMPUTER. (SPECOM` 2004), PROCEEDINGS.  S  428-432. 2. Gumenjuk A., Kostyshin A., Borisov K., Salnikova O. - On the acoustic elements of a poem and on the formal procedures of their segmentation // Glottometrics.-8(2004)- Liidenscheid: RAM- Verl.,S 42-67</p>

Aspect Oriented Programming  attempts to aid programmers in the separation of features, or the breaking down of a program into distinct parts that  overlap in functionality as little as possible.  </p>

 title : The meta-aspectj Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Meta-AspectJ is a language tool for generating AspectJ programs using code templates. MAJ itself is an extension of Java, so users can interleave arbitrary Java code with AspectJ code templates. MAJ is a structured meta-programming tool: a well-typed generator implies a syntactically correct generated program. MAJ promotes a methodology that combines aspect-oriented and generative programming. Potential applications range from implementing domain-specific languages with AspectJ as a back-end to enhancing AspectJ with more powerful general-purpose constructs. In addition to its practical value, MAJ offers valuable insights to meta-programming tool designers. It is a mature meta-programming tool for AspectJ (and, by extension, Java): a lot of emphasis has been placed on context-sensitive parsing and error-reporting. As a result, MAJ minimizes the number of meta-programming (quote/unquote) operators and uses type inference to reduce the need to remember type names for syntactic entities.</p>
 title : The midas-judge Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Midas is a Programming Competition System, oriented to competitions such as the ACM ICPC. We offer this as a (nearly) zeroconf alternative to PC^2. </p>

<p>We admire the CSUS PC2 team&#39;s work because it is a very complete piece of software, but we have also encountered some of its flaws. One of them -the one that give us most trouble- is the fact that PC2&#39;s implementation relies on Java&#39;s RMI. </p>

<p>RMI has huge requirements on network setup, which are not easy to comply with in most situations. This is why we want to offer a lightweight alternative written in .NET (using Remoting), so we can control its behaviour easily... </p>

<p>This project was initiated by a few Computer Science and Software Engineering students at Universidad de los Andes in Bogotá D.C., Colombia. </p>

<p>We chose the name Midas because in greek mythology he was the judge in Apollo&#39;s and Marsyas&#39; musical duel, and he was a very fair one (which earned him donkey ears in the end). It&#39;s common knowledge that he was very ambitious, and... Let&#39;s face it, everyone who enters a programming competition IS ambitious, right? </p>

 title : The nila Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Prototype for a dataflow programming language., </p>
 summary : <p>Novelties is a high-level declarative RPG programming language. It has a variety of features that model various aspects of an RPG game. It differs from other languages in that: </p>

<p>Novelties focuses on the high-level concepts rather then low level details. Low-level details can be specified as styles and is applied coherently cross scenes and actors. Novelties eases the development of RPG by providing a declarative and structural programming language. Novelties provides mechanisms for writing the script in various languages(as in i18n). For example, by programming appropriate header, you can write your script in pure Chinese in Novelties. Novelties is easy to learn even for people who have little programming experiences. Novelties is based on compiled JavaFX running on JVM, which provides strong support for i18n and various platforms. Novelties supports a DSL for defining maps that can be easily created and modified.  Novelties is still under heavy development and is not feature complete. Novelties is not just another programming language for RPG games. The goal for Novelties is to design and implement a programming language for RPG games that is simple, clean, and expressive(as opposed to complex, messy, and constrained). Any feature suggestions are welcome.</p>

 title : The pangolin-ml Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Here is a piece of software related to the paper: Extended Static Checking of Functional Programs </p>

<p>We present a Hoare logic for a programming language equipped with recursive, higher-order functions, algebraic data types, and a polymorphic type system in the style of Hindley and Milner. It is the theoretical basis for a tool that extracts proof obligations out of programs annotated with logical assertions. These proof obligations, expressed in a typed, higher-order logic, are discharged using off-the-shelf automated or interactive theorem provers. Although the technical apparatus that we exploit is by now standard, its application to functional programming languages appears to be new, and (we claim) deserves attention. As a sample application, we check the partial correctness of a balanced binary search tree implementation.</p>

 title : The pangolin-programming-language Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>OverviewThe Pangolin programming language is a functional language. In this language, the programmer can write logic assertions about the computed values. These assertions are proven statically, which ensures that the program is correct with respect to its specification. </p>

<p>InstallationRequirementsTo compile Pangolin, you need: </p>

<p>the latest Objective Caml compiler, ocaml-3.10. the latest version of menhir (tarball). the latest version of alphaCaml (tarball). </p>

<p>To handle proof obligations, Pangolin uses: </p>

<p>the latest version of Ergo. optionally the latest version of Simplify (in the ESC/Java package). the latest version of Coq. </p>

<p>InstructionsDownload the source code and follow the usual sequence: </p>

<p># ./configure
<br/># make</p>

 title : The luamm Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : No description has been added for this project.
<a href="/p/luamm/edit">Add description</a>
 summary : <p>Pointless Haskell has changed home. Please point your links at http://haskell.di.uminho.pt/wiki/Pointless+Haskell. </p>

<p>Pointless Haskell is a library for point-free programming with recursion patterns, inspired in ideas from the PolyP library. The syntax follows directly the theoretical one, with generic recursion patterns parameterized by the data type to which they should be applied. </p>

<p>It was developed as part of the PhD research by Alcino Cunha and has served as a base for the teaching of point-free programming in introductory courses to functional programming. </p>

<p>The library also features the visualization of the intermediate data structure of hylomorphisms with GHood. This feature, together with the DrHylo tool for deriving hylomorphisms from a restricted Haskell syntax, allows the easy visualization of recursion trees of Haskell functions. </p>

<p>This project reports the re-implementation of the whole library based on type-indexed type families, a recent Haskell extension provided by the Glasgow Haskell Compiler. </p>

<p>A related topic is point-free program calculation for the simplification and transformation of point-free functions. The automatic simplification of point-free Haskell programs can be performed with the SimpliFree tool, or with a more recent one-level transformation system (currently under development and available from the subversion repository) based on the same type families approach and developed under the 2LT project. </p>

<p>For more information consult the wiki pages.</p>

 title : The r-proto Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Perfection is achieved, not when there is nothing more to add, but when there is nothing left to take away.  — Antoine de Saint Exupéry </p>

<p>Inside every large program there is a small program trying to get out.  — CAR Hoare </p>

<p>Below on this page are sections on:  </p>

<p>IntroductionApplicationsNewsCitationAdditional InformationProto BugsAvoiding R Bugs </p>

<p>Introductionproto (google code name r-proto) is an R package which facilitates a style of programming known as prototype-based programming. Prototype-based programming is a type of object oriented (OO) programming in which classes and objects are unified into a single concept, prototypes.  This makes proto and prototye programming simpler than the usual OO model yet it retains the OO features of inheritance (known as delegation in the prototype model) and OO dispatch.  Applications, News, Additional Information sources, Proto Bugs and Avoiding R Bugs sections are given below while associated Links are in the Links box to the right. </p>

<p>ApplicationsThe following R packages use or are typically used with proto: </p>

<p>The R gsubfn package provides a generalization of the R function gsub for which the replacement string can be a function.  The replacement string can also be a proto object which holds the function as well as state information which can be carried from one function invocation to the next. ggplot2 is a grid based graphics package in R that uses proto internally.  (Also see this page for info on creating ggplot2 geom proto objects.) pmg is an R package that provides a GUI interface to R that uses proto internally. The gWidgets R package for user interface construction can be used in conjunction with proto as seen from the examples that contain the  word proto or scoping in this list.  Also see this r-devel post for another example of gWidgets with proto. gWidgetsWWW package is an implementation of gWidgets for the web that works with RApache on Mac and Linux (and under Windows using a virtual Linux machine). gWidgetsWWW uses proto internally. The ascii R package generates Docbook as well as output of other formats. It uses proto objects as the underlying container objects. The sqldf package allows R users to manipulate R data frames using SQL.  It uses proto internally. DescribeDisplay produces publication quality graphics from the output of the describe display plugin of GGobi. AlgoTrader is an R package that provides infrastructure for formally describing financial trading algorithms as well as facilities to test their performance.  The package allows backtesting and contains various reporting utilities. traitr is an R package for creating GUIs using the model/view/controller (MVC) paradigm. NewsMarch 12, 2010.  The Appendix of this document on AlgoTrader contains an introduction to proto that could be of interest to anyone wishing to use proto even if the Algotrader package is not applicable to their area. (This may have been there for some time but I just noticed it.) </p>

<p>March 2, 2010.  An example of a stack in proto was posted on r-help. </p>

<p>February 27, 2010.  Recently Duncan Murdoch discussed one aspect of R that he would prefer worked differently; namely, that objects were not ultimately looked up in the global environment.  If you are using proto you can emulate it.  The following are three different variations: </p>

<p>p Note the following R command which shows the R search path: </p>

<p>search()The first example starts at the second entry in the search list (which is why it omits the global environment).  The next example starts at the Stats entry in the search list and moves forward.  The last example starts right at the end of the search list thereby skipping over the rest of it and was suggested by Peter Daneberg in the same thread as appropriate in certain  circumstances. </p>

<p>Mar 7/08.  In the development version of proto the parent argument to the proto function may now be a function in which case its environment is used as the parent.  This facilitates constructing proxy proto objects: with(proto(f, f = f, a = 1), f) wedges an anonymous proto object between f and its environment inserting a into the proxy so that it can be accessed as a free variable from within f. </p>

<p>Dec 01/07.  Added a new argument, eval.env = parent.frame() to the proto function in the devel version of proto.  It defines the environment in which promises in the ... arguments are evaluated.  The default value of eval.env is normally what one wants; however, in the case of wrappers around proto one would generally want the calling frame of the wrapper rather than the frame which directly calls proto and this argument facilitates that. The need for this is related to the problem in R described in point #4 of Avoiding R Bugs at the end of this page. </p>
