<p>1. str.proto.  This will not affect most users but one user was redefining print and that caused name.proto (hence str.proto) to break.  The call to print has been replaced with a call to print.default in name.proto to avoid this in the devel version of proto.  Here are three workarounds in the meantime: Run this code: </p>

<p>name.proto or, source the new version of graph.proto.R which is the file that contains name.proto: </p>

<p>source(&quot;http://r-proto.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/R/proto.R&quot;) # load changed codeor, ensure that your proto object has a ..Name component.  For example, this works even if print is redefined: </p>

<p>print 2. A proto object could not have the name x. </p>

<p>Avoiding R BugsDue to the fundamental nature of proto, it makes use of portions of R that may not be commonly accessed in other packages; therefore, it has uncovered a number of R bugs or deficencies that were not previously known or at least are less known.  Fortunately there are simple workarounds to deal with them provided you know about them.  </p>

<p>1. LazyLoad </p>

<p>If a package uses lazyloading then R will erroneously change the class of all proto objects at top level to &quot;environment&quot;.   This r-devel post from the R development team confirms that it is a bug in R and that there is an intention to fix it (however, as of  &quot;R version 2.8.0 alpha (2008-10-01 r46589)&quot; it had still not been fixed.  See this r-devel post for details and info on how to test it.)  To avoid this bug use LazyLoad: false in the DESCRIPTION file of any package that has proto objects at top level.  </p>

<p>In older versions of R it was possible to use SaveImage: true in the DESCRIPTION file; however, SaveImage is not available in recent versions of R. </p>

<p>One gotcha is that not specifying LazyLoad is not the same as LazyLoad: false.  As mentioned in R News 4/2 if LazyLoad is not specified then R will use lazy loading if there is more than 25K of R code in the package and otherwise not.  See this: r-devel discussion.   There is some information on LazyLoad and SaveImage in this r-devel post and there is an article on lazy loading in R News 4/2.  (This behavior will change in R 2.9.0 where true will be the default and the odd 25K criterion will be eliminated.) </p>

<p>One can test this by creating an R package with only two files which are (1) this DESCRIPTION file: </p>

<p>Package: testlazy
<br/>Version: 1.0-0
<br/>Date: 2008-10-03
<br/>Title: Test lazy loading
<br/>Author: G Grothendieck
<br/>Maintainer: G Grothendieck 
<br/>Description: Test lazy loading with top level objects.
<br/>Depends: proto
<br/>LazyLoad: yes
<br/>License: GPL-2and (2) this R/testlazy.R file: </p>

<p>TopLevel We test it like this: </p>

<p>library(testlazy)
<br/>class(TopLevel)If the class of TopLevel is just environment then the proto component of the class has been stripped by R. </p>

<p>One related problem is that if you use LazyLoad: false to overcome the problem above then proto will not be available during the package load unless it is specifically loaded so add: require(proto) to your code if any top level proto objects are created at load time.  See: this r-devel post and this related post . </p>

<p>2. Promises and Lists </p>

<p>R is supposed to evaluate promises that are stored in lists but, in fact, it does not -- see this thread in r-devel.  It is currently believed that this has never affected the released version of proto on CRAN nor does it affect the most recent devel version of proto.  It did affect earlier devel versions of proto.   Even though it seems to currently have no consequence  we are leaving this item here just in case it comes up in some new form and needs to be revisited.  (This may be fixed already in the R 2.9.0 development version.) </p>

<p># No longer a problem but recorded here just in case.</p>

<p># ensure proto 0.4-0 is installed from Source tab 
<br/># or just load the CRAN version of proto and over top
<br/># of it source proto.R from the repository as discussed 
<br/># in the Sep 25th News item above
<br/># 
<br/># in the code below:
<br/># - p is a proto object 
<br/># - x a child of p created by invoking p$new
<br/># - y is a copy of x formed by converting the
<br/>#   the proto object to a list and back to proto
<br/>#
<br/># The problem is that although ls(y) says that gg is in y
<br/># when we try to evaluate it, R says its not there.</p>

<p>p 3. Subclassing environments </p>

<p>Operating locally on an environment attribute changes its value globally which seems undesirable. </p>

<p>The proto class is an S3 subclass of the environment class.  Unfortunately if e is a variable holding an environment and f is a copy of it then if you set an attribute on f then e gets it too: </p>

<p>f After the above e will gain attribute abc with a value of 3 as well.  This occurs even if 3 is assigned within a function. &quot;class&quot; is an attribute so it also applies to the class.   </p>

<p>4. Limitations on Use of Promises </p>

<p>Using pure R, there is currently no way to copy promises without evaluating them nor is there any way to discover the environment associated with a promise.    For the proto clone function it would be desirable to be able to copy promises without evaluating them while preserving their environments.  Although the preceding are not possible in pure R it is possible to do this using C. </p>

<p>This is no longer a problem in R but is being left here in case it comes up again in some other form. </p>

<p>In the code below test fails.  Note that this code does not use proto and this is a general problem in R. </p>

 title : The ropl Open Source Project on Open Hub
 title : The s-ma-u-g Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Finite State Machine IdentificationIdentification has been defined as an inference process, which deduces an internal representation of the system from samples of it&#39;s functioning. There are many possibilities to a represent system, one of them is to use a finite state machine (FSM).  </p>

<p>There are many applications for identification  in different fields such as logical design, verification or test, sequential learning. For example finite automata (FA) are useful models for many important kind of hardware and software systems (lexical analysis, system for verifying the correctness). </p>

<p>The modeling problem consists of researching the &#39;best&#39;  FSM (in practice, one of those that best describe the process behavior), which respects the dynamics of the external model. Finding a minimum size deterministic FA consistent with the set of given samples is NP-complete. </p>

<p>The genetic simulation approach is an alternative that reduces the complexity of the preceding methods. </p>

<p>Our goal is to create methods based on Genetic Algorithm (GA), which allow to find FSM using only external behavior. </p>

<p>This project uses a methodology based on genetic algorithms for inferring finite state machines. </p>

<p>Basic parameters like fitness functions and chromosomal representation that can be used with canonical genetic algorithm were defined. Different types of finite state machines can be infered. Several improvements were introduced: inner decimal representation has been used to improve the speed of initialization stage, post-processing stage has been used to remove unaccessible states. </p>

<p>Currently this project is a part of my PhD thesis. But originally it was developed during my MSc studies.</p>

 title : The scilab-mip Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Interfaces between scilab and: </p>

<p>GLPK (a real scilab interface not an interface which relies on mex); LPSOLVE (a real scilab interface not an interface which relies on mex); Coin-OR Clp + Cbc + IPOpt + Bonmin + Symphony. With such an interface, you can deal efficiently with huge problem (each library works with sparse matrix) and, with the Coin-Or library, you can reach the same level of performances as with a linear programming commercial tool. </p>

<p>For the CoinOR part: </p>

<p>CLP: is a C++ library dedicated to solve huge linear programs. Was before 2004 released as a commercial tool by IBM. This tool was named OSL. CBC: is a C++ library dedicated to solve huge mixed integer linear programs. IPopt: is a C++ library dedicated to solve non linear constrained optimization problems NLP). Bonmin: is a C++ library dedicated to solve non linear mixed integer constrained optimization problems (MINLP). Symphony: is a C/C++ library dedicated to solve mixed integer bicriteria linear programs. This library supports OpenMP (so it works efficiently under multicores) and PVM (and work nicely under parallel architectures). The parallel things are only supported on linux box. For windows, it&#39;s just a mater of having or not a visual express edition. The OpenMP library is not shipped with the visual express edition. </p>

<p>With the scicoinor toolbox, you can read / write easily MPS and LP files. </p>

<p>You can read some news related to the development of the tools. The changes to come are here too. </p>

<p>If you need some advices on how to compile the coin-or tools under linux, have a look at this page. </p>

<p>The list of MPS files shipped with the CoinOR toolbox. </p>

 title : The toolsdotnet Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>The purpose of this project is to combine and publish &quot;re-usable&quot; coding snippets that were encountered by this project authors during their .NET programming practice and made available to community in a form of lightweight libraries to share, discuss and improve. </p>

<p>Main ideas of this project until it officialy reaches its release milestone are expressed here: http://plainoldstan.blogspot.com. </p>

<p>Upon release following targets are expected to be satisfied: - No static dependencies on heavy libraries - 50% documentation - 80% code test coverage </p>

<p>Some review onto existing re-usable .NET frameworks will be given to explain the placement of this framework: </p>

<p>Existing re-usable .NET frameworksMicrosoft Enterprise Library, CSLA.NET, ACA.NET, Subsonic, Castle, Spring.NET,  dotNetNuke, Logging frameworks First focus and delivery of this project will be logging and hosting of wcf services. </p>

<p>Logging Using System.Diagnostics.Trace and System.Diagnostics.TraceSource in ASP.NET applications  Leverage WCF style of logging and tools  Introducing XmlWriterRollingTraceListener  Introducing DatabaseTraceListener  Interlacing WCF and your own logging  Dependency injection for TraceListeners and Filters  References Wcf HelpersWindows service host for Wcf Wcf Spring.NET integration Dependent on PLINQ and Parallel extensions framework progress, this project will may have nothing to say for the below at the release time, but so far it is still in the project&#39;s scope: </p>

<p>Batch and parallel processesWindows services helpers for long running cuncurrent processes Scheduling services Resilience services Unit of work Source control integration  </p>

 title : The workerpool Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Performing tasks in many threads made fun! </p>

<p>This module facilitates distributing simple operations into jobs that are sent to worker threads, maintained by a pool object. </p>

<p>It consists of these components: </p>

<p>Jobs, which are single units of work that need to be performed. Workers, who grab jobs from a queue and perform them. Worker pool, which keeps track of workers and the job queue. </p>

<p> </p>

<p>Getting StartedThe best place to start for now is to read the code and look at the examples in the unit tests (located under trunk/test/) and the sample uses (located under trunk/samples/). Documentation contributions are welcome! What have you accomplished with the workerpool? </p>

<p>Tutorials: </p>

<p>MassDownloader - How to write a simple multi-threaded mass downloader in under 10 lines of code. </p>

<p> </p>

<p>StatusThere&#39;s good work being done on a native Python multiprocessing module. The functionality has a lot of overlap with workerpool. Worth having a look at! </p>

<p>News </p>

<p>2008-03-09: Released workerpool 0.9.2 (CHANGES) Warning: WorkerPool constructor signature changed. 2008-03-02: Released workerpool 0.9.1 (CHANGES) 2008-03-02: Added MassDownloader tutorial. </p>

<p>Add more complete usage examples and wiki tutorials. More thorough unit testing Finalize the API for a 1.0 release </p>

 title : The ariah Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Ariah: Re-imagine the WebAriah is a JavaScript through which Web designers can deploy custom hyperlink relationships and client-side data format converters, in a way that remains accessible for unscripted browsers. For example, </p>

<p>    
<br/>      Release Notes       </p>

<p>Ariah detects that the author wants the linked resource included as inline XHTML, and that it requires conversion from Markdown format. So, Ariah downloads the file, converts it, and replaces the link with the results. If the browser cannot run Ariah, then the file remains accessible through a normal hyperlink. </p>

<p>Although Ariah implements several built-in hyperlink relationships like &quot;include&quot;, &quot;source&quot;, and &quot;template&quot;, Ariah also exposes a simple JavaScript API so Web programmers can more easily define their own custom relationships among Web pages, as well as their own client-side file format converters (called &quot;hyperformats&quot; in Ariah parlance). Ariah is the class name for the acronym of &quot;Accessible Related Includes and Ajax Hyperformats&quot;. </p>

<p>Ariah can use combinations of multiple relationships to help discern what to do with hyperlinks. For example, </p>

<p>    
<br/>      View the hf.js source code.       By adding the term source to the include relationship, the author is telling Ariah not to parse the file normally, but to show the original source text of the file. In this case, if Ariah can find a source formatter for files of type application/ecmascript, then the displayed result will use code-coloring; otherwise, Ariah will insert the source code of the script as plain text. </p>

<p>Ariah also works on head links. For example, </p>

<p>         When placed before Ariah&#39;s script element, Ariah will automatically load the &quot;client-side&quot; template file and apply it to the current Web page. Because the head section of the template will run, most recurring scripts, stylesheets, and repetitious design elements can be pruned out of each Web page and into a client-side template. Such a workflow simplifies Web design, streamlines a site&#39;s bandwidth, and usually improves accessibility. For example, the template file linked above can be an XHTML file with an empty body, but with a list of primary and alternate template links in its head section: </p>

<p>    
<br/>    
<br/>    
<br/>    
<br/>          
<br/>    
<br/>    
<br/>    In such an arrangement, a Web browser can select a template file most appropriate to the medium and a user interface most appropriate to the user&#39;s preferred mode. Each chosen template, in turn, can link to its own primary and alternate stylesheets. </p>

<p>Sites using AriahAriah is the next generation of some of my earlier work on client-side includes (c. 1996) and hyperformats (c. 2000) which were stable, but in its current form, Ariah is not. However, interested Web developers can see one of Ariah&#39;s ancestors, hf.js &quot;in the wild&quot; on the inner pages of http://grayschoolofmusic.com . The script itself is at  http://grayschoolofmusic.com/Scripts/js2/hf.js . The Gray site demonstrates many of the features discussed about Ariah, so feel free to view the source code of its pages.  </p>

<p>Future PlansBecause Ariah uses a &quot;markup interface&quot;, the Ariah project is planning to help implement native modules for Open-Source Web browsers to accelerate performance of Web pages designed for Ariah. The native modules should be able to activate automatically whenever they detect a link to Ariah script, so acceleration can happen transparently. As a side effect, native Ariah modules may make it possible for Web browsers to cache many popular script libraries in an optimized state to be transparently reused from many Web sites. For example, </p>

<p>    A native Ariah module might detect that the techst.js script can be loaded from a cached version with a matching title URI loaded from another site, so long as the digital fingerprint of the cached version matches the hash encoded at the URL in the title field. Otherwise, the file will be downloaded normally from the current host. </p>

<p>StatusAriah is still in a mid-alpha state under heavy development, so it should not be used in production work. This alpha release has only been tested under Firefox 2.0 and Safari 1.3 on Mac OS X, so it is likely to break other browsers until it goes through the crucible.  </p>

<p>Ariah is a symbiotic rewrite of some of my earlier code that was stable under the two latest versions of Internet Explorer, Firefox, Safari, and Opera, each on Windows, Mac OS X, and Linux, where available. I won&#39;t promote Ariah to beta status until it passes tests under each of those clients and platforms. </p>

<p>Ariah&#39;s alpha download bundles several test scripts that help demonstrate the features described here, with the exception of those described under the &quot;future plans&quot; heading. Several of these scripts are more interesting than Ariah itself, but available nowhere else. See the download&#39;s readme and script documentation for more details. </p>

<p>AuthorRich Hall</p>
 title : The axton Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>axton is a Cross-Browser JavaScript Web Application Framework whose goal is to provide an extremely object oriented vehicle for developing AJAX Web Applications. </p>

<p>Among the features currently present are </p>

<p>Extensions and simplifications to the DOM manipulations A simple Aspect Oriented Programming (AOP) library A global event management framework A rich AJAX framework that supports:  Queued message transport with multiple queues Automatic JavaScript Object Notation (JSON) and XML content negotiation Client-side response caching A quick syntax version for simple requests A Unit Testing package based on xUnit UI Component Framework (new in version 96) Menus Planned features include </p>

Though there is some dependency between components, it is very possible to assemble components into functional packages to minimize their size.  There are currently 3 such assemblies (as of version 95), all are minified: </p>

<p>axton-compressed.js : includes all features axton-base-compressed.js : includes some of the base functionality (without AJAX) axton-data-compressed.js : focused on basic AJAX (no DOM, no Caching, no unit testing)</p>
 title : The bija Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Bija, or (B)ija (I)sn&#39;t (J)ust (A)jax, is a high-quality, lightweight, efficient, and very network-oriented library of JavaScript. It abstracts away important features such as  Object Oriented Programming and DOM Manipulation, as well. </p>

<p>It currently supports: - IE6  - IE7 - Gecko  (Firefox/Mozilla) - WebKit (Safari) - KHTML  (Konqueror) - Opera </p>

<p>Unlike other JavaScript libraries, Bija doesn&#39;t limit its Ajax portion to just XMLHttpRequest. Bija supports a wide variety of useful network functions, such as HTTP Streaming, Remote XML Documents, and more.</p>
 title : The cidades-estados-js Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>UpdateSaiu do forno a nova versão 1.0 estável na qual não é mais preciso criar selects obstrusivos. Agora você pode implementar o cidades-estados-js em inputs (type text) ou qualquer outra tag. Veja a implementação do script funcionando. </p>

<p>GeralA intenção deste projeto é colocar sempre em um único lugar um arquivo javascript que pode ser utilizado em qualquer site para criar duas combo-box (em html, select) com escolha de estados e cidades. </p>

<p>Decidi hospedá-lo no servidor do google porque assim é mais improvável que hajam problemas de servidor em qualquer servidor que eu hospede. Para instalá-lo em seu site, coloque a seguinte instrução entre suas tags head. </p>

<p>Feito isso, a biblioteca está instalada em seu site. O legal é que todos os sites que usarem esta biblioteca usarão o mesmo provedor/servidor. Gravando no cache do usuário o mesmo arquivo, sendo assim, carregado mais rapidamente na próxima vez que o usuário acessar qualquer outro site que tenha referencia para o mesmo arquivo. </p>

<p>Para ativar a biblioteca você pode utilizar os próprios métodos do javascript ou o dgDomReady da biblioteca ou mesmo qualquer biblioteca como prototype, mootools ou jQuery. </p>

<p>A forma mais simples de ativar a biblioteca é esta, usando o objeto dgCidadesEstados passando os objetos que serão serão usados como select de estados e cidades. Veja um exemplo: </p>

<p>window.onload = function() {
<br/>  new dgCidadesEstados({
<br/>    estado: document.getElementById(&#39;estado&#39;),
<br/>    cidade: document.getElementById(&#39;cidade&#39;)
<br/>  });
<br/>}
<br/>dgDomReadydgDomReady é um evento auxiliar que executa uma determinada função quando o objeto DOM é carregado. A diferença básica entre window.onload e dgDomReady é que o window.load é executado quando a página é carregada por completo, com as imagens em anexo e os arquivos flash. Já o dgDomReady é executado quando apenas o arquivo html é carregado, sendo assim, mais rápida a execução do que no outro caso. O exemploanterior ficaria assim: </p>

<p>window.onDomReady(function() {
<br/>  new dgCidadesEstados({
<br/>    estado: document.getElementById(&#39;estado&#39;),
<br/>    cidade: document.getElementById(&#39;cidade&#39;)
<br/>  });
<br/>});
<br/>Aplicações usando sua biblioteca preferidaEm jQuery, o mesmo exemplo poderia ser explicado por: </p>

<p>$(function() {
<br/>  new dgCidadesEstados({
<br/>    estado: $(&#39;#estado&#39;).get(0),
<br/>    cidade: $(&#39;#cidade&#39;).get(0)
<br/>  });
<br/>});
<br/>Prototype: </p>

<p>Event.observe(window, &#39;load&#39;, function() {
<br/>  new dgCidadesEstados({
<br/>    estado: $(&#39;estado&#39;),
<br/>    cidade: $(&#39;cidade&#39;)
<br/>  });
<br/>});
<br/>Recuperando os dadosPara fazer o sistema recuperar uma informação dada anteriormente, basta passar os parâmetros estadoValue e cidadeValue dentro do construtor. </p>

<p>new dgCidadesEstados({
<br/>  cidade: document.getElementById(&#39;cidade2&#39;),
<br/>  estado: document.getElementById(&#39;estado2&#39;),
<br/>  estadoVal: &#39;SP&#39;,
<br/>  cidadeVal: &#39;São Paulo&#39;
<br/>});Ou então passando como atributo value em sua tag select (ou input como descrito mais abaixo). </p>

<p>new dgCidadesEstados({
<br/>  cidade: document.getElementById(&#39;cidade1&#39;),
<br/>  estado: document.getElementById(&#39;estado1&#39;)
<br/>});Obstrusividade?! Não!Não é preciso que você escreva uma tag select, você pode executar usando um input que será substituido pelo select necessário. Para ativar esta opção, basta passar o parâmetro change. </p>

<p>new dgCidadesEstados({
<br/>  cidade: document.getElementById(&#39;cidade3&#39;),
<br/>  estado: document.getElementById(&#39;estado3&#39;),
<br/>  change: true
<br/>});Charset?!Você não precisa se preocupar em codificação de caracteres, o cidades-estados-js é disponibilizado nas versões Latin (ANSII) e UTF-8. Para isso, basta alterar a forma como você chama a biblioteca. </p>

<p>Dê preferencia a usar o charset utf-8, mas se seu sistema não aceitar essa codificação ou você usa DreamWeaver e nem sabe o que é isso, provavelmente você vai precisar da versão em ASCII. ;D </p>

<p>Nota: Vale a pena ler o artigo sobre intercacionalização de caracteres da w3c que explica mais sobre codificação, inclusive o utf-8. </p>

<p>updateNa versão 0.2 podemos pedir para o plugin inseir os valores de estados quando carregar o plugin. Para isto, basta inserir um terceiro parâmetro (true) na criação do objeto. </p>

<p>Usando como base a função cifrão ($) como: </p>

<p>function $(elm){
<br/>  return document.getElementById(elm);
<br/>}Chamamos a função de inicialização assim. Onde o true indica que queremos que sejam preenchidos os estados automaticamente. </p>

<p>new dgCidadesEstados($(&#39;estado&#39;), $(&#39;cidade&#39;), true);todoAutomatizar o estado e cidade. Assim a cidade e o estado aparecerão já marcados com um único comando. </p>

<p>Criar os devidos elementos, assim pode-se criar a partir de inputs text para gerar os selects dinamicamente, acabando com o problema de javascript desabilitado. </p>

<p>Implementar plugin para Dreamweaver.</p>

 title : The dewind Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Kingfishers - 在线演示 : http://dewind.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/kingfishers/example.htmKingfishers - 最新下载 : http://dewind.googlecode.com/files/Kingfishers-1.0.1.rar      </p>

<p> </p>

<p>Kingfishers是一个用javascript语言编写的,能够代替alert,在浏览器中连续输出客户端javascript脚本运行日志的工具。
<br/>主要用于客户端脚本的分析和查错。
<br/>Kingfishers是本人在学习javascript的过程中写的一个练习作品.还有很多地方需要完善,试用后欢迎您反馈好的创意.
<br/>自己为工具起的名字是 kingfishers(翠鸟),寓意它将精致的栖息于您的项目中.
<br/>kingfishers-1.0版雏形发布后,依旧会致力将它做的更加简单实用,力求完美无暇。
<br/>Kingfishers 新闻中心v1.0.1发布[2008/11/21]
<br/>v1.0.1改进的功能如下:</p>

<p>1.新增三个参数
<br/>moveborder = true   //(可选)拖动及调整日志Console大小时是否出现虚线框 是:true(默认)/否:false
<br/>grayout = true      //(可选)拖动日志Console时,底层页面元素是否灰显 是:true(默认)/否:false
<br/>targetdiv=&quot;targetDivId&quot;   //(可选)将日志Console嵌入到指定id的div中 </p>

<p>2.扩充$Log.url接口
<br/>Kingfishers-1.0   : $Log.url({url地址})
<br/>Kingfishers-1.0.1 : $Log.url({url地址},{代码高亮风格});
<br/>使用方法形如：
<br/>$Log.url(&#39;http://www.baidu.com&#39;,&quot;html&quot;);
<br/>$Log.url(&#39;http://dewind.googlecode.com/files/kingfishers-1.0.css&#39;,&quot;css&quot;);
<br/>$Log.url(&#39;http://dewind.googlecode.com/files/Kingfishers-readme.txt&#39;);
<br/>$Log.url(&#39;http://ovsmbt.mop.com/ov.js&#39;,&quot;js&quot;);  </p>

<p>3.针对每条logger日志的处理
<br/> 单击: 该条日志所在行变为蓝色背景,此时清除信息动作将忽略此条日志.
<br/> 双击: 该条日志的内容被选中,直接按ctrl+c,可将日志内容拷贝到剪贴板中.</p>

<p>4.在logger.js中加入以下方法:
<br/>function $alert(message,color){
<br/>   $Log.loginfo(message,color);
<br/>}
<br/>5.结合$FT.show()功能,增加错误栈输出.</p>

<p>6.整合example
<br/>v1.0.0 发布[2008/11/05]1.浏览器兼容: IE, Mozilla Firefox, Opera ,Safari,Chrome
<br/>2.XHTML 兼容: XHTML 1.0 Transitional、XHTML 1.0 Strict 、XHTML 4.01 Transitional、XHTML 4.01 Strict

 title : The duroty Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Duroty is a service of personal feeds, email management, link management and briefly it will also include electronic calendar and server file indexation.</p>

<p>Duroty is addressed to SMEs which need information and knowledge management systems in order to diminish the barrier to the access to information.</p>

<p>It uses simple and advanced message searching systems similar to the ones used by Google webs, but it also allows to search in attached files (word, powerpoint, excel, pdf, html, etc.) in addition to the normal fields such as from, to, subject, body, etc.</p>

 title : The erlyjs Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>ErlyJS is a Javascript compiler running on and compiling for the Erlang virtual machine. </p>

<p>Motivation:Short answer: For highly scalable and lightning fast serverside Javascript. Long answer:  The ultimate goal is to simplify the process of building Ajax and Comet Web applications. ErlyJS should help to achieve this by allowing the same programming language for server and client side. There is not much choice for that programming language, Javascript is the only one running natively in web browsers. To run Javascript at serverside there are existing solutions (Rhino, Spidermonkey) but for better horizontal scalability, performance, fault tolerance and ease of deployment, the multi-core and high-concurrency Erlang virtual machine has been chosen and a Javascript compiler had to be developed from scratch. ErlyJS should provide full interoperability with Erlang, so web frameworks and Web / Application servers written in Erlang can be used. Implementation details:Leex/Yecc based grammar Compiler generates byte code for the Erlang VM Option: recompilation only if source has changed (compiled Javascript modules store source checksum) Compatibility:Javascript version: 1.5 Spidermonkey/Rhino: global function load  Project status:Pre-alpha. Right now a major refactoring is taking place to move the code base from erl_syntax based approach to Core Erlang. The code in SVN trunk is out of date, git is used now and repo URLs will be announced here once the refactoring to Erlang Core is complete  </p>

<p>ToDo:Add all the missing stuff to provide full Javascript support, comparable to Spidermonkey and Rhino Implement native serverside Browser DOM support  Implement AST parse transformations for: pretty-printing Javascript source code safely shrinking Javascript source code refactoring Javascript source code Implement API for Javascript debugging, profiling and code analysis Wanna contribute ?You are familiar with Erlang, Javascript, Lambda Calculus, Parsers and Lexers: you are the most wanted ! You know Javascript, but not Erlang: write Javascript tests</p>

 title : The flexible-javascript-unittest Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Flexible Javascript Unittest Framework中文说明见：http://pickerel.javaeye.com/admin/blogs/277775 </p>

<p>A tiny yet flexible javascript unit test framework, feature: </p>

<p>1.Support synchronize and async test.
<br/>2.Customizable  test results ui.
<br/>3.Expandable assertion mechanism.usage1.basic usage: </p>

<p>window.onload = function(){
<br/>    var test1 = new testcase(&quot;my firest test&quot;, {
<br/>        setup: function(){this.val = &quot;abc&quot;;},
<br/>        teardown: function(){this.val = null;alert(&quot;test completed.&quot;);},
<br/>        test_get_name: function(){
<br/>            this.assert_equal(&quot;abb&quot;, this.val, &quot;test get name&quot;);
<br/>            this.assert_not_equal(&quot;abb&quot;, this.val);
<br/>        }
<br/>    };
<br/>    test1.run();
<br/>}2.test asyn methods: </p>

<p>function xhttp(url, callback)
<br/>		{
<br/>    if (typeof XMLHttpRequest != &#39;undefined&#39;) {
<br/>        httpRequest = new XMLHttpRequest();
<br/>    }
<br/>    else if (typeof ActiveXObject != &#39;undefined&#39;) {
<br/>        httpRequest = new ActiveXObject(&#39;Microsoft.XMLHTTP&#39;);
<br/>    }
<br/>    httpRequest.open(&#39;GET&#39;, url, true);
<br/>    httpRequest.onreadystatechange = function () {
<br/>        if (httpRequest.readyState == 4) {
<br/>            callback(httpRequest.responseText);
<br/>        }
<br/>    };
<br/>    httpRequest.send(null);			
<br/>}	
<br/>window.onload = function(){
<br/>    var test1 = new testcase(&quot;my firest test&quot;, {
<br/>        setup: function(){this.val = &quot;abc&quot;;},
<br/>        teardown: function(){this.val = null;alert(&quot;test completed.&quot;);},
<br/>        test_get_name: function(){
<br/>            this.assert_equal(&quot;abb&quot;, this.val, &quot;test get name&quot;);
<br/>            this.assert_not_equal(&quot;abb&quot;, this.val);
<br/>        },
<br/>        test_get_name1: function(){
<br/>            this.assert(false);
<br/>            throw &quot;this is an exception&quot;;
<br/>        },
<br/>        async_test_google: function()
<br/>        {
<br/>            var self = this;					
<br/>            xhttp(&quot;http://www.google.com&quot;, function(html){
<br/>                self.assert(html.indexOf(&quot;google&quot;) &gt; 0);
<br/>                self.complete();
<br/>            });					
<br/>        },
<br/>        async_test_yahoo: function()
<br/>        {
<br/>            var self = this;					
<br/>            xhttp(&quot;http://www.yahoo.com&quot;, function(html){
<br/>                self.assert(html, &quot;google&quot;);
<br/>                self.assert(html.indexOf(&quot;yahoo&quot;) &gt; 0);
<br/>                self.complete();
<br/>            });					
<br/>        }			
<br/>    });
<br/>    test.run();
<br/>}    faq1.how can i do async test? </p>

<p>  a.the test method name must start with &#39;async_test_&#39;
<br/>  b.call this.complete() when the async method is completed.2.how to custom the output ui? </p>

<p>create a new testcase_ui object and implement the methods: </p>

<p>    var myui = function(test){
<br/>        this.test = test;
<br/>        this.on_inited = function(){};
<br/>        this.on_assert_success = function(assert_name, method_name){};
<br/>        this.on_assert_failed = function(assert_name, method_name, default_message, message){};
<br/>        this.on_error = function(method_name, e){};
<br/>        this.on_completed = function(test){};	
<br/>    }</p>

<p>    then attatch it to the testcase with:
<br/>        new testcase(&quot;name&quot;, {...}, new myui());
<br/>    or
<br/>        var test = new testcase...
<br/>        test.ui = new myui();3.support assertions: </p>

<p>    assert
<br/>    assert_equal
<br/>    assert_not_equal
<br/>    assert_null
<br/>    assert_not_null
<br/>    assert_match
<br/>    assert_not_match     4. how to add my own assert method? </p>

<p>it&#39;s easy to do, just add the method as below: </p>

<p>   testcase_assertion.prototype.assert_blabla = function(...)
<br/>    {
<br/>        //var default_msg =  &quot;actual is not null&quot;;
<br/>        //var bool = (actual == null);
<br/>        //this.do_assert(&quot;assert_null&quot;, bool, msg, default_msg);	
<br/>    };</p>

<p>  // Load the latest version of the Google Data JavaScript Client
<br/>  google.load(&#39;gdata&#39;, &#39;2.x&#39;);</p>

<p>  function onGoogleDataLoad() {
<br/>    // Put your code here
<br/>  }</p>

<p>  // Call function once the client has loaded
<br/>  google.setOnLoadCallback(onGoogleDataLoad);</p>

<p>Place any code that uses the JavaScript client in the onGoogleDataLoad() function.  Continue reading to learn more and to see examples. </p>

<p>DocumentationHere&#39;s an overview of how to use the JavaScript Client.  There are more details about each JavaScript class available in the JavaScript Client Reference.  If you&#39;d like to learn more about the Google Data APIs in general, visit the Protocol Basics guide (v2.0).  title : The js-hcalendar Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>hCalendarhCalendar is a microformat for embedding semantic calendaring data in XHTML. </p>

<p>What does that actually mean? It means that something like this: </p>

<p>  
<br/>    
<br/>      May 21, 2005
<br/>      (2 hours)
<br/>    
<br/>  will render as plain text that is legible by humans reading your page, and is at the same time completely machine-parsable.  hCalendar uses the concepts of iCalendar (the data format behind Apple&#39;s iCal, among other things), but allows &#39;events&#39; to be embedded in ordinary HTML pages using standard HTML tags. </p>

<p>js-hcalendarjs-hcalendar is a simple JavaScript program which, when included in a webpage, searches it for hCalendar events and builds a table-based visual calendar. It then inserts that calendar into a  that you put in your page. You should then style it with your choice of CSS; I&#39;ve created calendar.css and minicalendar.css as examples. </p>

<p>It is  very simplistic: it  entirely ignores everything but  the start date and the summary of the event; it doesn&#39;t even deal with the start time. But it is easily extendable. </p>

<p>(js-hcalendar was once known as JSCalendar, but that name overlaps with another excellent and unrelated project.) </p>

<p>DemosYou can look at a simple demo of a few random events. Note the links to switch between the two style sheets, if your browser does not support style-sheet switching. Or try a list of holidays from one of the first hCalendar sites, http://suda.co.uk/projects/holidays/, with JSCalendar injected.</p>

It takes one line of code to bind/unbind a hot key combination. </p>

<p>Example:Binding &#39;Ctrl+c&#39; </p>

<p>$(document).bind(&#39;keydown&#39;, &#39;ctrl+c&#39;, fn);Unbinding &#39;Ctrl+c&#39; </p>

This should be solved in the next version More infoPublic Git Repository at GitHub Live Demo Read More...</p>

<p>mvn installor wait for the next stable version. It would not be long. Thank you. </p>

<p>This project is evolving and more interesting. </p>

<p>The Jscombiner (JavaScript Combiner) is a helper tool which will help you to manage your javascripts.  </p>

<p>Imagine this case. You got a javascript project directory like this: </p>

<p>web_app
<br/>|    index.jsp
<br/>|
<br/>\---scripts
<br/>    |   config.js
<br/>    |   app.js
<br/>    |
<br/>    \---pkg
<br/>            a.js
<br/>            b.jsHere the config.js is a optional file which provide configuration information. app.js is kind of main application script. </p>

<p>Inside app.js: </p>

<p>/**
<br/> * @import pkg.*
<br/> */
<br/>// any code herepkg/a.js and pkg/b.js are some kind of functions or classes scripts. </p>

<p>Then, what do you expect in the index.jsp? </p>

<p>...And what about adding a pkg/c.js? You can update index.jsp by hand. </p>

<p>But what about you got dozens of scripts, dozens of applications and you have to update one or two of them in the complicate hierarchy? </p>

<p>To avoid this issue, many developer keep a small volume but long scripts. But this is not good to manage your code and collaborate. </p>

<p>Jscombiner will help you get through of this. See the @import in app.js comment. All you should do is adding dependencies description. Then, let Jscombiner do the rest using a tag-lib: </p>

<p>...Also, Jscombiner has a command line tool to combiner your scripts into a big script. </p>

<p>Jscombiner is so beta, examples and docs are on the road. But if you are eager, just let me know via leegorousatgmail.com or raise an issue. </p>

<p>Saving your time is saving the world. </p>

<p>Enjoy! </p>

<p>Below is the old description, it works all the time. </p>

<p>Managing javascripts is not a nice job and it will get worse as your scripts grow quickly. JSC (JavaScriptCombiner) comes to set you free on it. </p>

<p>You can organise your scripts as you want, write down the configuration and let JSC do the rest. </p>

<p>JSC can assemble your scripts into one js file, generate an agent page and testCase pages (JsUnit test page) according as the configuration file. </p>

<p>JSC is developed in Java. </p>

<p>在开发JavaScript项目中，管理js是一个比较令人头疼的问题，特别是当项目快速发展，脚本越来越长，越来越多时，增删修改在所难免时，管理问题凸显。 </p>

<p>为此制作这个小工具来让我们可以以所希望的粒度来分布和组织脚本文件，但又不会使得管理他们成为一种负担。 </p>

<p>设想我们有很多脚本，这些脚本有些可以独立成模块的，但有些则不好独立，但是在管理上，做好功能区分是更加有利的，于是开始拆分这些脚本为单独的脚本。又或者我们希望脚本是以类（跟Java的类概念相近，但是是prototype型的）为单元的，那么将一个类独立成一个文件管理起来会更加方便。拆分成大量的独立脚本之后，又如何组织起来呢？按照最基本的办法，就是写大量的脚本引用标记，又或者像某些脚本导入框架所使用的方法一样进行动态导入。然而问题是当脚本数量比较多时，手动进行比较费事失事，客户端需要装载大量小脚本，而且脚本是顺序执行的，也就是说有依赖关系的，搞清关系这个本身也比较麻烦。这个就是JavaScriptCombiner（简称jscombiner，或者JSC）的最初的开发目的。 </p>

<p>JSC最基本的功能就是安装配置文件，读取脚本，组织好其依赖关系之后，合并成一个大脚本（未压缩）。而JSC怎么知道应该如何去处理那些关系呢？答案是脚本需要提供其依赖信息，例如加入形如下面的注释： </p>

<p>/**
<br/> * @import net.leegorous.jsc.*;
<br/> */但是可以预见的是，每次修改脚本都需要重新组装一次脚本，这个有点不好，于是为其增加一种模式，agent模式，专门用于调试的。其原理就是生成一个agent页面，读取并组织好关系后不是将脚本写入agent页面，而是将每个脚本相对于agent页面的引用标记写入。外部页面以一个iframe包含（其实也可以不包含而直接使用）agent页，这样在脚本发生修改之后就不需要重新合成，因为每一次装载都是直接调用小脚本本身，这在（本地）调试时几乎看不出有影响。 </p>

<p>再就是测试脚本的需求，JSC提供了对Edward Hieatt开发的JsUnit的支持。使用者只需要像JUnit一样为testCase建立一个脚本，脚本里面包含所需要的依赖信息，在配置文件里面需要指明jsUnitCore.js所在的目录并且指明testCases所在的位置，JSC就能够为每个testCase脚本生成可以在JsUnit中运行的测试页。 </p>

<p>JSC的功能目前还比较简单，但是在实际使用过程当中，觉得它真的可以节省不少劳动时间，于是拿出来大家分享一下。:P</p>

 title : The jsmud Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>jsmud - JavaScript MUD KernelAbout jsmudThe JavaScript MUD Kernel is software which allows developers to build a fully working MUD server utilizing the JavaScript scripting language. The project does not provide a ready-to-run MUD system, but instead requires that developers implement their own MUD from scratch. All that jsmud provides is the necessary networking, timer, and data storage APIs to the JavaScript environment. </p>

<p>The jsmud project was originally written as a proof-of-concept in the course of two days by Sean Middleditch of Mojodo, Inc.  Several more days of effort have been put in since then.  There is much left to do before jsmud is ready for prime time. </p>

<p>jsmud does not run inside of a web browser!  jsmud embeds the SpiderMonkey JavaScript engine inside of a conventional server process.  It has nothing to do with web browsers, HTML, or client-side JavaScript application development. </p>

<p>InstallationThere is no installation required for jsmud. Simply unpack the jsmud-0.5.tgz tarball and run make: </p>

<p>tar -zxf jsmud-0.5.tgz
<br/>cd jsmud-0.5
<br/>makeThe file named README has information on development using jsmud. </p>

<p>Latest versionThe latest release is jsmud 0.5. This is a pre-release not intended for serious development! </p>

<p>DiscussionUse the jsmud group at Google Groups to discuss the development and usage of jsmud.</p>

 title : The php-javascript-css-aggregator Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>This project does 2 major things: 1. It makes sure you include every css and js only once in every page you generate. This is very helpful when using templating, since you want to attach the template css to the template, but if you reuse the template the css will be called several times, not necessarily causing any damage, but there is a slight performance hit, and problems in firebug (and we don&#39;t want that!) 2. If you set $GENERAL_CONFIG&#39;aggregate&#39; = true, then this code starts aggregating the css and js files into one large file. This helps decrease calls to http, really boosting up your site&#39;s performance. </p>

<p>USAGE: 1. Create the cache table (see notices) 2. Create the code accessing the cache table, basically this is a class supporting the functions $db-&gt;GetCacheInfo, $db-&gt;SetCacheInfo, and $db-&gt;CreateCacheInfo. 3. require js_css_aggregator in your code, and either call js_include_once(), or css_include_once() as necessary. 4. to output the cache into your html, the code provides the global variables $all_js and $all_css, which you just echo in your html. To provide the best performace for your site, echo $all_css at the top of your html, and echo $all_js at the bottom of your html. </p>

<p>NOTICES: 1. To use the aggregator you need the following db table: CREATE TABLE cache ( </p>

<p>id int(11) NOT NULL auto_increment, 
<br/>cache_name varchar(100) collate utf8_unicode_ci NOT NULL, 
<br/>cache_content text collate utf8_unicode_ci NOT NULL, 
<br/>version varchar(100) collate utf8_unicode_ci NOT NULL, 
<br/>last_update datetime NOT NULL, 
<br/>last_update_unix bigint(20) unsigned NOT NULL default &#39;0&#39;, 
<br/>PRIMARY KEY  (id), 
<br/>UNIQUE KEY cache_name (cache_name) 
<br/>) I didn&#39;t add the database code to the project yet because it is too customized for the project I wrote the aggregator for. So this google code is for php programmers not afraid to hack and customize code to fit their own projects. I am hoping that in the near future I will have a quiet weekend to turn this code into a closed component. 2. The code currently creates a different cache per page, but that is easily modifiable.  3. There is different code producing the js and css includes, but they are virtually identical, I will probably pretty up this code when I have the time. </p>

<p>WISHLIST: 1. Wrap this code in a normal class to get rid of the horrible global variables. 2. Split the parameter $GENERAL_CONFIG&#39;aggregate&#39; into $GENERAL_CONFIG&#39;js-aggregate&#39; and $GENERAL_CONFIG&#39;css-aggregate&#39;, so people can choose whether they want to aggregate js or css only. 3. Add the database code to the class so people don&#39;t have to write it themselves. 4. That someone would either volunteer to help me with this, or that someone will take this and rewrite it into something more useful for the community :)</p>

 title : The dragon-game-engine Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>The Dragon Game Engine will be a BSD licensed game engine plus tools.  The software will be developed using C/C++, Java, and some scripting languages to be determined (currently considering Python and Lua).  The initial development roadmap aims to allow for the creation of tile-based games presented using ASCII text.  The initial target platform will be Microsoft Windows on x86 processors.  This will be the 1.0 milestone.  Future steps will be taken to port the engine to *nix-based operating systems on the same processors (and potentially OS X).  The next major milestone will be adding non-ASCII based 2D graphical support for Microsoft Windows, followed by ports to *nix operating systems (and again potentially OS X).  The next major milestone will be adding support for 3D graphics for Microsoft Windows, with ports following for other operating systems.</p>

 title : The google-game-platform Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>google-game-platform is a distributed web-based online game platform which use Google resources including Google Talk, Google Base and Google Page Creator. These are the features as bellows: </p>

<p> No real physical server facilities are required. All the basic services required by an online game are provided by Google services. 2. Game content and static data are stored in Google Page server. 
<br/>3. Game runtime data are stored in Google Base server. 
<br/>4. User accounts are managed by Google Talk (GMail) server. Only friends can join a game. 
<br/>5. The game content is easy customized by users. </p>

<p>Planning features in the future if possible: </p>

<p> User can go through game groups by trust mechanism. For example, in a RPG game, a user go through game groups just like from one country go to another country. 2. The game list can be embedded in the Google Talk Client. </p>

<p>There is a test page which proved the technical possibility on my Google Page http://kctan.tw.googlepages.com/TestChatClient.htm. It is modified from a simple flash example: Animation. User can move the “tofu” object by the cursor then broadcast the new position to all other clients by Google Talk. All the other clients can see the real-time moving effect of the “tofu”. There are the requirements: </p>

<p> IE 6.0 (only tested in this browser) 2. Flash Player 8.0 
<br/>3. JRE 6 
<br/>4. A Googl Talk (GMail) account 
<br/>It uses java applet including smack to commutate between flash and Google Talk Server. Be careful that it will broadcast the messages to all the clients on your Google Talk client users for now.</p>

 title : The lost-cities-game Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>This project is my Java implementation of the fantastic 2-player card game called &quot;Lost Cities&quot;, invented by the prolific German game designer Reiner Knizia. At the moment, you can only play against the computer (and a pretty weak game it plays too). Future enhancements may include human-human games, a player ladder, and a high score table. </p>

<p>I wrote this game in early 2001 in order to learn Java, with a view to becoming a professional software developer. Although it succeeded at that, looking back at the code with the benefit of seven years&#39; commercial Java experience makes me shudder and cringe. There are a lot of things I&#39;d like to refactor, such as: </p>

<p>converting the reference data from int constants to Java 5 enums abstracting the AI out of the rest of the code to make it pluggable properly separating the domain logic (e.g. game rules) from the GUI code </p>

<p>The program deliberately uses some of the newer features of Java (e.g. Swing). So in order to run it as an applet, you may need to download an appropriate Java Runtime Environment (JRE) from Sun&#39;s web site. This will be a one-off process. If a new enough JRE is already installed, the game will start up straight away. </p>

<p>The game has a Help menu that explains both the rules of the game and how the program works.  </p>

<p>If you discover any bugs or have any suggestions on how the program or the computer&#39;s play could be improved, please email me at andrew dot i dot swan at gmail dot com. </p>

<p>Lost Cities is a game of very simple rules but fascinating depth - enjoy!</p>

 title : The reversi-game Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Scope of the project is to develop the game based on a grid with eight rows and eight columns, played between you and the computer, by adding pieces with two sides: black and white.  </p>

<p>At the beginning of the game there are 4 pieces in the grid, the player with the black pieces is the first one to place his piece on the board.  </p>

<p>Each player must place a piece in a position that there exists at least one straight (horizontal, vertical, or diagonal) line between the new piece and another piece of the same color, with one or more contiguous opposite pieces between them. </p>

 title : The textadventuregameeditor Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>Rules and how to playThere is a grid. Two players step by step places their dots(each player has it&#39;s own dot color) on free positions of the grid. The goal of the game is to surround partner&#39;s dots with your own dots. More exactly, the goal is make amount of surrounded dots as much as possible.  </p>

<p>Compile/RunRequirement: Qt 3.3.3.  </p>

<p>You can use either Makefile(generated by qmake) or Visual Studio project to build and run the game. </p>

<p>Currently game runs only on Windows. However there are no platform-specific restrictions, so you can easily port it to any Qt compatible platform.</p>

 title : The turb-game Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>TurbTurb is a (2D) multi player gravity dogfight game where you control a rocket and try to make life as short as possible for your antagonists with a small arsenal of weapons. It&#39;s heavily inspired by the best multi player game for the Amiga: Turboraketti II. </p>

<p>It supports 2 players locally using split screen and/or multiple network clients. </p>

<p>It&#39;s written in Python using Pygame and still work in progress but still quite playable and there is a map editor to make creating your own maps easy.</p>

 title : The wetsrc Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>This is Kriss  and this is shi  . </p>

<p>We make games, this small collection of seemingly random projects are all games development related and released here for your inconveniences. </p>

<p>WetPlay : a flash xspf MP3 player, built using MTASC and SWFMill </p>

<p>SGSS : a simple games website written in php only without using any databases. This uses the Mochi games feed as the source of games. </p>

<p>The projects that are intended to be open source are being shifted slowly over from my personal svn repository that can be found at https://trac.xixs.com/ Please note that not everything you can find there is going to be explicitly licensed and moved. I just try to keep as much of my source code visible there that I reasonably can so it is available for reference if not free use.</p>

 title : The ancienttales Open Source Project on Open Hub
 summary : <p>I love the good old RPGs like Ultima, DDD (german RPG from the 80&#39;s) or Angband. </p>

<p>The target is a fairly complex item, skill and NPC model that is loosly based on DSA (again a german system) and D&amp;D. </p>

<p>Another goal is to create a small world with few NPCs but the possibility to load quests. This way I can offer a free game and charge you for quests (hey, just joking). </p>

<p>One great motivation is OOTS. I LOVE OOTS. It&#39;s great. You have to read it before you play the game, otherwise your character dies instantly! </p>

<p>The game is implemented under Windows using wxWidgets. I have my reasons.</p>
